Molotov Advocates: Increase Soviet Russian Armaments: Central Executive Committee Plenary Session Opens 36

Moscow – Molotov, Chairman of the Soviet Russian People's Committee, today called for an increase in Soviet Russian armaments. Molotov based his argument on the news of the Japanese-German alliance, which he said threatened Soviet Russia. Molotov also gave a comprehensive overview of the world situation, harshly criticizing Japan, Germany, Poland, and Italy. He also stated that the sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway demonstrated Soviet Russia's strong desire for peace, but Japan's refusal to sign a non-aggression pact and its unwillingness to form a committee to mediate disputes arising from the Soviet-Manchukuo border showed Japan's warmongering spirit. Regarding Germany, Molotov considered it to be an armed camp that threatened all of Europe. Molotov further said that the news of the German-Japanese military alliance was expected, as both countries had withdrawn from the League of Nations and both harbored aggressive ambitions. Molotov predicted that Soviet Russia would thrive this year. (National Telegram, 10th)

Moscow – The plenary session of the Second Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union opened today at the Kremlin. The Grand Hall of the palace was filled with representatives and guests. When Stalin, Kalinin, Molotov, Voroshilov, and other party and government leaders stepped onto the podium, they were greeted with enthusiastic applause that lasted for quite some time. Kalinin delivered the opening address, and Molotov gave a lengthy report on the 1936 national economic plan. The diplomatic corps attended the opening ceremony. (TASS dispatch, 11th)

US Senate Foreign Relations Committee Discusses New Neutrality Law: Continues Investigation of Morgan Company 37

Washington – The Senate Foreign Relations Committee recently met to discuss the new Neutrality Act. It obtained the consent of Secretary of State Hull to delete a clause that would prohibit the shipment of certain goods to belligerent nations. This clause stipulated that if the President believed that the shipment of any goods that could be used for war to a belligerent nation would prolong the war, then he should prohibit their export. Some people criticized this clause, saying that it would closely link the United States with the sanctions imposed by the League of Nations, and that once the League of Nations passed a ban on the export of oil, the United States would have to participate. Therefore, the Senate Foreign Relations Committee deleted it. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Washington – The Senate Munitions Investigating Committee is continuing its investigation into how the Morgan bank provided financial assistance to the Allied Powers before the United States entered World War I. Morgan testified again today. Senator Clark, a member of the committee, said that in 1915, the Morgan bank stopped supporting the British pound, causing a panic in the foreign exchange market, and that its intention was to pressure the US government to accept loans to the Allied Powers. Morgan denied this. Clark then read a letter from Morgan to a certain branch office, which stated that on August 19, 1915, the British mail ship Arabic was sunk by a German submarine, and two American passengers were drowned, which greatly angered the United States and helped with the then-existing proposal to loan to Britain. Morgan admitted that this incident did indeed increase American sympathy for the Allied Powers and create a more favorable atmosphere for loans to Britain. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Washington – Details of the Senate Munitions Investigating Committee's questioning of the Morgan bank have already been sent in a separate telegram. Here are more details. Committee members stated that at the time, Britain had issued bonds totaling $500 million, but had been unable to sell them all. Therefore, the Morgan bank forced American manufacturers to purchase them. Senator Clark also read a letter from Morgan to the British branch office, stating that Britain should ask American manufacturers to purchase British bonds and use British purchases of American goods as a condition for exchange. Morgan replied that at the time, he had not forced American people to purchase British bonds. He also said that the claim that the US government's change in its neutrality policy and its loans to Britain were influenced by the Morgan bank was not true, and that "some people attack New York bankers, saying that they should be directly responsible for America's entry into the war. I specifically deny this statement." The committee then adjourned until Monday of next week. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Washington – Morgan, the internationally renowned banker, faced the Senate Munitions Investigating Committee today with a calm demeanor, and enthusiastically denied that the Morgan Company manipulated foreign exchange in 1915 and forced the US government to lend money to the Allied Powers through debt. Before the committee members could ask questions, Morgan stood up and said, "The committee clearly has a preconceived notion that we created the foreign exchange market panic in 1915. I want to deny that the Morgan Company ever had this intention." Senator Clark stated that because of the Morgan Company's assistance, the British pound was withdrawn, causing disruptions to America's booming wartime trade. The purpose was to force President Wilson to act. This is clearly evident from the documentary evidence. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

Isolated in Naval Conference: Japan Considers Policy: Drafting Instructions for Delegation: Cabinet Meeting Final Decision Today 38

Tokyo – The Ministry of Foreign Affairs convened a leadership meeting on the morning of the 11th to discuss the government's draft instructions. In the afternoon, it was submitted to a joint conference of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of the Navy. The content is roughly as follows: The Japanese representatives should make efforts to explain the Japanese government's disarmament policy, with setting a common maximum limit system as a condition, advocating the total abolition of offensive weapons. Furthermore, they should sincerely explain Japan's attitude towards preparing for the total abolition of battleships, aircraft carriers, and Class A cruisers. The Japanese government does not want to express any opinion on the fact that the four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and the United States do not recognize Japan's disarmament policy, excluding the issue of quantitative limitations, and opening a four-country conference. However, since this is the case, they believe that the five-country disarmament conference will definitely conclude, and the four-country conference will start again. Japan will maintain a non-immediate, non-separated attitude towards this four-country conference. Regarding the issue of establishing a separate regulation restricting the use of submarines, and two or three other supplementary issues, based on past relations, they should be reviewed at the five-country conference, and there are no particular objections. (Domei dispatch, 11th)

Tokyo – The Navy Department maintains its views on the instructions requested by the London delegation. The disarmament conference has no meaning to continue, so it requested an early vote on the success of the Japanese proposal, preparing to withdraw from the conference. For the four-country conference, observers can be sent to attend. (Domei dispatch, 11th)

Tokyo – The government will hold an extraordinary cabinet meeting at the Prime Minister's official residence at 1:30 PM on the 12th. Navy Minister Osumi and Foreign Minister Hirota will explain the contents of the instructions issued to the Japanese delegation in London. After the cabinet formally decides, Foreign Minister Hirota will send these instructions to the delegation. (Domei dispatch, 11th)

Japanese Delegation Requests Instructions: Naval Conference at Final Stage 39

Tokyo – The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, based on the request for instructions from the Japanese delegation in London, explained the course of the past conference and presented the opinions of the plenipotentiary representatives. The content is as follows: The Japanese delegation has made its best efforts, but the situation has reached its final stage. The Japanese side strongly advocates continuing to discuss quantitative limitations, but Britain claims that its shipbuilding notification plan is part of the quantitative limitation issue. The United States, France, and Italy also expressed sympathy with Britain, and a situation of opposition to Japan has arisen. Britain seems to intend to discuss the quantitative issue again after reviewing the notification plan, but this is not what we can expect. The Japanese delegation expressed opposition to the above-mentioned procedural matters. The four countries of Britain, the United States, France, and Italy will request our side to send observers to attend the conference. If we refuse, the four countries will continue the conference. Should Japan send observers? Please request instructions in reply. Also, how about ordering France and Italy to participate in the fourth section of the London Treaty, restricting the use of submarines, and making it a separate regulation? Please request instructions in reply. Japan should consider this situation, request the conference to declare a recess, or participate in the review of the notification plan, and wait for the re-examination of the quantitative issue. When the conference turns into a four-country conference, what attitude should be taken? Please urgently request instructions. (Domei dispatch, 11th)

Japanese Representatives Seek Outcome: Naval Conference Repeatedly Postponed: British Government Consults with Dominions 40

London – It has been learned that the naval conference originally scheduled to be held on Monday has been postponed to Tuesday. This was requested by the Japanese delegation because the Tokyo Cabinet will consider this matter tomorrow. At the same time, representatives from Britain and its overseas dominions are currently meeting to discuss the policies that the British Empire must adopt after Japan withdraws from the conference. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

London – Efforts are currently being made to retain Japan in the naval conference. At the same time, representatives from Britain and its dominions met this afternoon at the Foreign Office to discuss the policies that the British Empire delegation should adopt if Japan withdraws from the conference. The Japanese delegation requested a discussion of its naval equality proposal. Today, the British chief representative, Navy Minister Monsell, agreed to postpone the exchange of shipbuilding program proposals at the naval conference on Monday and listen to the Japanese representatives' views on a common maximum limit and make a public announcement on this. The opposition attitude of other delegations is well known, so Japan's withdrawal from the conference can be predicted. After Japan withdraws from the naval conference, the conference will continue by the four countries of Britain, the United States, France, and Italy, or Russia and Germany will be invited to join. As for the procedures to be followed thereafter, they have not yet been determined. The general idea is to pass a mutual exchange of shipbuilding program proposals and agree on some qualitative restrictions, such as reducing the size of battleships and cruisers. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

London – Regarding the invitation of Russia and Germany to participate, naval officials said that this naval conference was only attended by representatives of the signatory countries of the Washington Naval Treaty and the London Naval Treaty, namely Britain, the United States, France, Italy, and Japan. The invitation of representatives from other countries has never been considered, but if the proposed five-nation naval agreement cannot be reached, then it should be discussed separately. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

London – According to this agency's correspondent at the naval conference, the British and American delegations have both accepted changing the conference procedure and will re-discuss the common maximum quota issue proposed by Japan on Monday. The reason for this is to take the opportunity to clearly explain the point that they cannot accept Japan's demands. Some people believe that the confrontation between Japan and the United States is the reason for the failure of the naval conference. This can be clearly demonstrated by the attitude adopted by Britain and the United States. It should be known that the principle of common maximum quota held by Japan is not only opposed by Britain and the United States, but also by Italy and France. It is now believed that once Japan announces its withdrawal from the conference, the naval conference will continue by the four countries of Britain, France, Italy, and the United States. The four delegations generally agree that this approach will enable the resolution of some technical issues. In addition, other countries, such as Germany and Russia, may be invited to participate, but before the four-country conference is actually held, a six-country conference is unlikely to become a reality. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

London – It seems that the United States is absolutely unwilling to accept the principle of common maximum quota proposed by Japan. Although Britain also fundamentally opposes it, it may eventually be willing to compromise and start a more extensive study of Japan's claims. Today, the British delegation consulted with various national delegations separately. It is reported that it asked the French delegation to persuade the Japanese representatives to change their attitude and not remain so rigid, in order to extend the time of the conference. Britain's attitude is actually afraid that the naval conference will divide the camp and place Japan in an extreme position, which would hinder political talks between the two countries in the future. Therefore, it is eager to avoid this. As for the Japanese delegation, it is currently awaiting new instructions from its government. If these instructions are as rumored, their nature will cause the naval conference to come to an end. However, some optimists still hope that the new instructions from Tokyo can at least allow the naval conference to continue its last gasp. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

London – Britain and the United States today agreed to abandon Japan and France and Italy and continue the London Naval Conference. This decision is the result of the five-nation conference reaching a stalemate after Japan proposed a common maximum naval limit. The complete failure of the conference is becoming increasingly inevitable, so Britain and the United States are taking this step and isolating Japan. According to reliable sources, British Foreign Secretary Eden warned the Japanese chief naval representative, Admiral Nagano, that Japan's unwillingness to compromise may affect Britain's Far East policy. (National Telegram, 10th)

London – The Daily Mail recently criticized the future of the naval conference, saying, "Britain, the United States, and Russia are all Pacific powers. Although their convening to conclude a Pacific agreement seems surprising on the surface, it is not impossible in reality. If the situation develops in this direction, then Japan's attitude towards the naval conference may change within the last minute. But it is still uncertain." The newspaper also said that the naval conference was originally composed of five countries: Britain, the United States, France, Italy, and Japan. Once Japan withdraws, Germany and Russia may join and become a six-country conference. This has already been explored. The British government invited the ambassadors of Germany and Russia to the reception for the delegations to the naval conference on Thursday for this reason. "As for Germany's attendance at the six-country conference, it is still hesitant, while Russia is prepared to participate. The superficial goal of this conference is to negotiate a temporary agreement to limit the maximum tonnage of various warships and to exchange shipbuilding information between the countries concerned. However, with representatives from Britain, the United States, and Russia gathered in one place, and with the Japanese representatives having withdrawn on their own, it is not impossible for various issues in the Pacific and the Far East to be discussed in the conference." (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Roosevelt: Establishes Agricultural Policy: Preserve Fertility and Manage Production 41

Washington – After the Supreme Court ruled the Agricultural Adjustment Act illegal, President Roosevelt spoke to reporters today about rural problems, saying that rural areas are a difficult problem for the country and that he felt it was his responsibility to treat it as a difficult problem. He decided to deal with this problem by preserving soil fertility and managing production. "We must avoid any national agricultural policy that could result in transferring the country's soil fertility abroad." This statement implies disapproval of subsidies. When speaking, President Roosevelt carefully avoided discussing any concrete plans, only saying that he wanted to seek legislation during this Congressional session to fulfill his responsibility to farmers. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

Washington – President Roosevelt has extended the effective period of the clause in the Gold Reserve Act establishing a stabilization fund for one year. When President Roosevelt announced this, he said that the emergency situation that existed when this bill was signed on January 30, 1934, had not yet been eliminated by international monetary agreements, and that in all respects, there were signs of its increasing weight, because the situation of international commerce and foreign exchange rates were not calm. President Roosevelt also extended the power, which is about to expire, granted to the President by the May 12, 1933 Act to stipulate that the weight of the gold dollar cannot be less than half of the legal weight at the time, nor more than 60% of the legal weight. However, this announcement did not mention changing the gold dollar's 59.06-base plan. President Roosevelt added that this announcement extends the President's power to reduce the value of the gold dollar. After consulting with Attorney General Cummings, according to Hengjie's interpretation, this announcement does indeed extend the President's power to devalue the currency. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

Washington – The House of Representatives today passed a bill authorizing the immediate payment of cash bonuses to 3.5 million veterans, in amounts ranging from $1 billion to $2 billion. The bill passed by a large majority of 355 to 59, and has since been sent to the Senate. A conflict will now arise between the President and Congress. If the Senate also passes it, President Roosevelt may veto it, but it is expected that Congress will override the President's veto by a majority vote. Supporters of this bill in the House of Representatives include members of both the Democratic and Republican parties. The bill does not mention the source of the necessary funding. Members of Congress who advocate inflation are now supporting this bill, so that new currency can be issued with the gold reserve in the treasury as collateral to pay for this bonus. This bill is a compromise between those who advocate inflation and those who advocate issuing public bonds. As for whether to adopt inflation or issue public bonds, the government will be free to choose. Judging from this bill, the trend of inflation has at least temporarily disappeared, because the supporters of Bateman's proposal to issue $2 billion in new banknotes have now agreed that if the majority of the House of Representatives does not support this bill, then they will not continue their efforts. However, one thing to note is that Congress may not support any proposal to increase taxes to raise money for the bonus. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

Sino-American Trade Situation Last Year 42

Washington – The Department of Commerce announced today that in the first eleven months of 1935, China had a trade surplus with the United States of $22,197,000, compared to a trade deficit of $23,788,000 in the same period in 1934. This was due to the fact that the United States imported a total of $57,234,000 worth of goods from China, an increase of 40% compared to 1934, and exported a total of $35,037,000 worth of goods to China, a decrease of 45% compared to 1934. Experts say that this has indeed reduced the burden on China's exchange rate stabilization, but the remittances from overseas Chinese to their homeland and other donations have decreased, which may offset this trade surplus. However, since the Chinese Yuan has recently appreciated, these remittances may continue to increase. China was in the process of reforming its currency in November of last year, but it was still able to maintain a trade surplus, which is a good sign for China's future. (National Telegram, 10th)

Wardha, India – Gandhi, the leader of the Indian National Congress, has recently been suffering from high blood pressure, but after doctors extracted two infected teeth, his condition has improved slightly. The doctor ordered him to take a long period of rest. According to today's doctor's report, there has been continuous progress over the past week, and yesterday his blood pressure dropped to its lowest level this week. Gandhi is quite weak due to malnutrition and prolonged bed rest, but he is in good spirits and sleeps well at night. According to the doctor, progress has been evident and there is no cause for concern at present. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

Japanese Fiscal Policy: Tax Increase Not Yet the Time 45

Tokyo – The Ministry of Finance held a meeting at 3:00 PM on the 10th, attended by Vice Minister Ritsushima and the heads of the relevant bureaus and sections. They reviewed the contents of the draft fiscal policy speech that Finance Minister Takahashi will deliver on the day the parliament reopens. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM. The content first explained in detail the draft budget for the 11th year of Showa, and reported on the current domestic economic situation, trade matters, and international balance of payments. What is noteworthy is that it mentioned the tax increase issue, saying that according to the current national situation, a huge amount of national defense spending is needed externally, and due to frequent disasters in recent years, rural areas are impoverished, and a large amount of funding has to be spent internally. Therefore, it is difficult to expect a reduction in national spending. However, considering all kinds of matters, now is not yet the time to implement a tax increase. Therefore, the revenue shortfall has to be made up for by public bonds. (Domei dispatch, 11th)

British Military Deployment in the Near East: Defensive Posture, but Substantial Troop Increase Demonstrates Resolve to Defend Ocean Routes 47

The disposition of British troops in the Near East, specifically in Alexandria, is clearly defensive rather than offensive. However, the recent increase in garrison strength and other preparations are sufficient to demonstrate Britain's determination to protect Egypt and imperial lines of communication against enemy incursions. The only route for an enemy attack from the west is along the coast from the border town of Sollum to the port of Alexandria. Egyptian camel corps soldiers are now stationed day and night in the sand dunes between the border and Sollum, watching for enemy movements. Italian soldiers are perched on rooftops and fortresses, surveying the desert with telescopes. In the current situation, no army in the world is capable of reaching the port of Alexandria from the west. Moreover, the Bedouin tribes of the western desert are not favorably disposed toward Italy. A Reuters correspondent spoke today with Italian officers outside the barbed wire barriers at the border; they all scoffed at the idea of an Italian attack. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

London: According to Lieutenant General Knox, the British supplementary reserve should have a strength of 165,000 men, but it currently numbers only 125,000, a significant shortfall. The British supplementary reserve undergoes weekly military training and periodically receives longer periods of training in military camps, specifically for the defense of mainland British territory. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Cairo: Another unit of British regular troops arrived here today. Four more battalions are expected to arrive by January 16. It is said that this troop movement is directly related to the student riots that have occurred here in recent weeks. (National Telegram, 10th)

Paris: Yugoslav sources announced today that the French and British fleets will indeed encircle Italy before the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting on January 20. It is claimed that a decision has been made to station nineteen British warships in the Yugoslav naval port of Split on the Adriatic coast. At the same time, other British warships will visit other ports such as Catalonia. The French fleet is currently busy loading coal and ammunition in preparation for major exercises, first in Corsica and then in the South Atlantic. (National Telegram, 10th)

London: As far as this agency's reporter knows, the British government is now trying to bring the East African war to a swift end. This is not solely for the sake of success in the League of Nations' policies, but also for the sake of Italy. In the near future, Italy may become an important factor in maintaining the balance of power in Europe, and it cannot be allowed to deplete its economic and military strength any further due to colonial affairs. Vasconcelos, chairman of the League of Nations' Committee of Eighteen, will convene the committee when the Council of Thirteen meets on the 20th of this month to discuss the oil embargo issue. Political figures here believe that the government will authorize Foreign Secretary Eden to support Vasconcelos' proposal. Generally, after the Committee of Eighteen meets, it will appoint several experts to submit detailed reports on the following: 1. Investigate Italy's oil reserves; 2. Estimate Italy's oil consumption during the Abyssinian rainy season; 3. Investigate the amount of oil that can be shipped to Italy from America. Once the experts' reports have been submitted, the Committee of Eighteen will further inquire whether the implementation of an oil embargo can immediately stop the East African war under the current circumstances. If it can, then for the sake of preserving Italy's strength, the Committee of Eighteen may even vote to pass the embargo measures. (Havas dispatch, 10th)

Geneva: The League of Nations Administrative Council is scheduled to meet on the 20th of this month. The League of Nations Committee of Eighteen will also meet on the same day, and its chairman, Portuguese representative Vasconcelos, will raise the issue of tightening the oil embargo against Italy. Regarding the oil embargo issue, no decision is likely to be made until the U.S. Congress passes the new Neutrality Act. League of Nations officials believe that even if the Committee of Eighteen and the Council of Thirteen hold meetings before the Administrative Council meeting, it would be useless. Therefore, the chairmen of the committees, Vasconcelos and Madariaga, both advocate holding meetings concurrently with the Administrative Council. League of Nations officials consider this aspect to be of great importance. The task of the Committee of Eighteen is to discuss sanctions against Italy, while the Council of Thirteen seeks a peaceful resolution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Paris: The renowned left-wing journalist Thibaud today wrote an article predicting the possibility of a renewed resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian issue, with the following main approaches: 1. Italy would request the League of Nations to appoint a neutral committee to go to Abyssinia, ostensibly to inspect Italy's methods of warfare, but in reality to study the possibility of reconciliation; 2. Belgium would suggest to the League of Nations that it appoint a Council of Thirteen to establish a kind of peace plan, mainly based on the joint development of Abyssinia by Britain, France, and Italy, while maintaining the Abyssinian Emperor's sovereignty over Abyssinia; 3. Efforts would be made to persuade the Abyssinian Emperor to request assistance from the League of Nations, and then the League of Nations would suggest to the Abyssinian Emperor that he employ British and French experts to study ways to improve Abyssinia's social, economic, and financial status. Thibaud also predicted that Britain and France might lend money to the Abyssinian Emperor to develop the entire country and subdue tribal chiefs who have been ambiguous in their attitude towards his rule. On the other hand, an Italian spokesman declared today that if the League of Nations is prepared to correct the errors of the Treaty of Versailles, then Italy is prepared to attend the next League of Nations meeting; if no satisfactory results are achieved, then Italy must completely conquer Abyssinia. (National Telegram, 10th)

Paris: An international affairs reporter for the 'Business News' recently learned that the major powers believe that if an African nation were to defeat a major European power in the Italian-Abyssinian War, not only would the balance of power among European nations be affected, but the peace and order of various colonies would also be endangered. The following methods are now being considered to seek a swift resolution of the Italian-Abyssinian dispute: that the League of Nations, at the request of the Italian government, organize a fact-finding committee to send to Abyssinia to investigate the Italian army's methods of warfare; after the investigation, to seize the opportunity to draft a peace plan and submit it to the League of Nations. This peace plan should not only emphasize Italy's needs, but also affirm the necessity of European assistance to Abyssinia. The reporter also learned that the Belgian government has submitted a proposal to the League of Nations Council of Thirteen to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, advocating that the Abyssinian Emperor personally request the League of Nations to entrust Britain and France to jointly study with the Abyssinian Emperor the necessary plans to improve Abyssinia's economic situation; when Britain and France assist Abyssinia, they should invite the League of Nations to participate in cooperation, and this improvement plan should be financially supported by Britain and France. (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Fascist Cadre Meeting Postponed; Abyssinian Army Captures Twenty-Four Tanks 48

Rome: The Fascist Grand Council, originally scheduled to meet on January 18, has now been postponed to February 1, to see what results from the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting on January 20. The Italian cabinet is scheduled to meet on January 30, and the Supreme Defense Council on February 4. According to responsible sources, Italy considers the oil embargo to be a very serious matter, but we will regard it as an "act of war." It has not yet been possible to ascertain (Reuters dispatch, 11th).

Munich: Although officials deny reports of large numbers of Italians fleeing into Germany and Austria to evade military service in East Africa, the Associated Press reporter learned today from several northern Italian residents that about two thousand Italians have already fled. Anti-Italian sentiment is most intense in the Tyrol region, where military authorities have been forced to go house-to-house to forcibly draft men into the army. Last September, nine Tyroleans were reportedly executed in Frankfurt for refusing to be drafted. (National News Agency dispatch, 10th)

Addis Ababa: It is raining heavily in Abyssinia. According to elderly people, such heavy rain at this time of year has never been seen before. Judging from various weather signs, it may not clear up for some time. It is generally believed that this is very beneficial to the Abyssinian army. Today, according to eyewitnesses to the battle of the Quina Pass, Abyssinian patrols overlooking the pass from the mountains saw several Italian tanks stopped in a valley below. They urgently summoned reinforcements and, after dusk, stealthily descended the mountain carrying huge rocks, blocking both ends of the valley, preventing the tanks from entering or exiting. At dawn, the Abyssinian army attacked in dense formation. The Italian army opened fire, but although dozens of Abyssinian soldiers were killed or wounded, they eventually surrounded the tanks due to their superior numbers, and shot down the Italian soldiers in the tanks. After an hour of fighting, the Italian army was unable to hold out and surrendered. According to the Abyssinian army, they captured ten tanks in this battle. In total, the Abyssinian army has captured twenty-four tanks, of which only one was damaged and cannot be repaired. The Abyssinian army's general headquarters has sent specialized technicians to inspect them and train soldiers to use them, to form the initial Abyssinian tank unit. (Reuters dispatch, 11th)

Lindbergh Kidnapper to be Executed by Electric Chair 49

New York: Bruno Hauptmann, the killer of Charles Lindbergh Jr., is scheduled to be executed in the electric chair on January 17. Meanwhile, Dr. Condon, who had previously been the intermediary between the kidnapper and Lindbergh, suddenly departed for South America this afternoon. It is claimed that he now needs a long period of rest, so it is difficult to predict when he will return to the country. At the same time, according to news from Trenton, New Jersey, Governor Hoffman has requested that a magazine retrieve the original manuscript of an article written by Dr. Condon, detailing everything about the Hauptmann case, for his review. It is claimed that the article is very relevant, but Hoffman is unwilling to explain his reasons for requesting the manuscript. (Reuters dispatch, 10th)

International Commercial Telegram 50

Reuters Special Commercial News, January 11

Gold and Silver: British Gold - The London gold price today was 140 shillings and 11 pence. American Silver - The opening price in the Montagu Silver Market remained unchanged.

Exchange Rates: The feature of this morning's foreign exchange market was the renewed weakness of the U.S. dollar. Western Shandong Suffers Heavy Losses in Floods; Zhengza Tax Revenue in Ten Counties Decreases by More Than 700,000; Four-Fifths of School-Age Children in Jining Drop Out of School 67

Jining Correspondence: Last year, the Yellow River breached its banks in Juancheng, flooding half of western Shandong and affecting counties in northern Jiangsu. Half a year has passed, but the breach has not yet been closed. Shandong Province established a county administration construction experimental zone, which includes fourteen counties in western Shandong. Ten of these counties were affected by the disaster. Many victims fled to other places for food. They had hoped to harvest wheat this spring to prolong their lives. However, it has been reported that the ice formed by the recent Yellow River floodwaters has melted again, and the water level has risen again, submerging the planted wheat. The devastation is complete, and it is feared that the region will not recover its vitality for ten years. Taking Jining as an example, there are currently only 82 elementary schools in the county, a decrease of two-thirds compared to before (mostly due to closures caused by the floods). Educational expenses are more than 48,000 yuan, a decrease of six-tenths compared to before. The former People's Education Center has been converted into a citizen's school. There are more than 50,000 school-age children in the county, but only over 9,000 are currently enrolled, and over 40,000 have dropped out of school. As for construction, the automobile road from Jining to Jinxiang, Yutai, and Jiaxiang has been washed away by the water and has not yet been restored. The county's telephone line, which runs from Jining county seat south to Tankouji, Tangkou, and Heshangqiao, has also been destroyed. The dikes on the county's rivers have been severely damaged by the Yellow River water, and the riverbeds have been silted up with Yellow River mud and sand, reducing their drainage capacity. Future autumn and summer rainy seasons will likely bring unavoidable floods. One county is like this, and the others can be inferred. Therefore, the water disaster has caused extraordinarily heavy local losses, unprecedented in its scale. Sun Zerang, director of the Heze branch of the Shandong Provincial Rural Construction Research Institute, has come to Jining to welcome Li Shuchun, director of the Civil Affairs Department. According to Sun, one-third of Heze county was affected by the disaster. The rural agricultural school had graduated three classes, totaling six thousand people, who have all retired to their home villages. Other counties have also graduated three classes, numbering two to three thousand people. During this water disaster, there were no reports of banditry in the countryside, thanks to the self-defense efforts of the students of the rural schools. Now that the weather is warm, the ice formed by the Yellow River water has melted again, and the water level is the same as during last year's major flood. Spring wheat planted in Heze, Juye, and other counties has been submerged again. The Experimental Zone Governor's Office has compiled detailed statistics on the collection and exemption of Zhengza taxes in the ten disaster-stricken counties and four non-disaster-stricken counties under its jurisdiction, as follows, to show the terrible extent of the disaster.

Geologist Ding Wenjiang Dies of Poisoning in Hunan; Ordered to Hunan to Investigate Geology; Hospital Complies with Instructions to Perform Autopsy 68

Changsha Correspondence: Geologist Mr. Ding Wenjiang, dispatched to Hunan to investigate mining, suddenly suffered coal poisoning in Hengyang. He was rushed to Xiangya Hospital for treatment, but medical treatment was ineffective. He unfortunately passed away at 5:45 PM on the 5th. Mr. Ding was a world-renowned geologist. His death is not only a great loss to the Chinese scientific community. The details of his poisoning, medical treatment, and death are recorded in detail below:

Details of Poisoning: Mr. Ding was dispatched to Hunan a month ago to investigate geology. He stayed in Changsha for several days and then traveled by car to Hengyang, where he stayed at the residence of a friend. However, feeling excessively fatigued from the journey, he took a small dose of sleeping pills and went to bed to rest. A servant of his friend, fearing that the cold air in Mr. Ding's bedroom would cause discomfort and that hospitality would be lacking, tightly closed the windows and filled the stove with coal to burn and ward off the cold. When they asked Mr. Ding to breakfast the next morning, they unexpectedly found that Mr. Ding had already suffered coal poisoning. His breathing had stopped, with only a faint breath at his heart. They immediately hired a Western doctor in Hengyang to treat him with artificial respiration and urgently telegraphed Xiangya Hospital, requesting that a doctor be sent to administer treatment. Zhu Jingnong, the Director of the Hunan Education Department, was a close friend of Mr. Ding. Upon hearing the news, he immediately accompanied Wang Zihuan, the President of Xiangya Hospital, Yang Jishi, the Director of Internal Medicine, and others to Hengyang in a special car. Although Mr. Ding was resuscitated after several hours of artificial respiration, he had been poisoned for more than eighteen hours. Moreover, when artificial respiration was administered, the doctor rubbed his ribs with both hands, causing severe injury. Therefore, Zhu, Wang, Yang, and others decided to take him to Xiangya Hospital for treatment.

Details of Treatment: After Mr. Ding was admitted to Xiangya Hospital, President Wang Zihuan and Director Yang Jishi took charge of the consultation. Miss Jue, the head nurse of the hospital, was assigned to oversee nursing. Four additional experienced nurses were selected and placed under Miss Jue's command. Miss Jue, a Westerner, took great care of Mr. Ding. She personally bathed Mr. Ding and provided him with all kinds of precious items he needed for his diet. However, although the coal poisoning Mr. Ding suffered gradually subsided, the rib injuries he sustained during treatment in Hengyang eventually became inflamed, and the wound discharged pus. After the doctor incised and removed the pus, the remaining toxins were not easily cleared, and the brain suffered severe stimulation as a result, ultimately leading to the failure of medical treatment. Thus, this world-renowned geologist, who once shook the world, passed away.

Autopsy Performed: When Mr. Ding was bedridden in Xiangya Hospital, knowing that his illness was serious and difficult to cure, he instructed the doctor that after his death, he wished to have his body dissected by the hospital. Mr. Ding, as a scientist during his lifetime, maintained his respect for science even in death. Therefore, all the doctors at Xiangya Hospital performed an autopsy at 11 PM last night in the Xiangya Medical Grand Auditorium. Medical students and faculty of Xiangya also participated. The autopsy results proved that the cause of Mr. Ding's death was the excessive force used during artificial respiration when he was poisoned in Hengyang. The hospital has already drafted a report, which will be released to the public soon.

Family's Grief: Since Mr. Ding passed away in Xiangya, his family, including his wife, Mrs. Shi, and his younger brothers, Wenlan and Wenhao, were by his side. Their grief was extraordinary. Mrs. Shi wept over the body, almost wanting to follow him to the grave. Wenlan and Wenzhi tried to maintain a calm demeanor, but reason could not overcome emotion, and their inner grief was evident in their tears. It is said that Mr. Ding's parents both died before the age of fifty. Mr. Ding, who was now over fifty years old, knew that he would not live long. He had already written his will the year before last, entrusting all his affairs to his wife, Mrs. Shi, and his younger brothers, Wenlan and Wenzhi. Now, unfortunately, it has become a reality. Those who suffer from coal poisoning are usually most numerous in the north. Mr. Ding served in the north for a long time but was not poisoned. Instead, he was poisoned in Hengyang. Is there truly a master in the dark?

Foreign Consuls' Concern: The consuls of the United Kingdom and the United States stationed in Hunan, regarding Mr. Ding as a world scholar, expressed deep concern for him after he became bedridden in Xiangya. They frequently inquired about his condition and telegraphed their respective governments without sparing expense, demonstrating the importance attached to Mr. Ding by various countries around the world. Upon hearing of Mr. Ding's death, they expressed condolences and lamented it as a great loss to the scientific community.

Chaoshan: Private Smugglers Devise All Kinds of Schemes; Negotiations Fail after Ronin Rob Cargo Ship; Untaxed Goods Still Actively Transported In 69

Shantou Correspondence: After ronin from a certain country intercepted and robbed a customs enforcement ship on December 17th last year, the Shantou Municipal Government lodged a serious protest with the consul of that country stationed in Shantou. The consul of that country initially prevaricated, and only at the end of last month did he formally reply to the municipal government in an official document, denying the interception and robbery, claiming that the smuggled goods were the goods of merchants of that country, which had been mistakenly taken by the customs enforcement team and had been returned by the customs authorities. He also stated that among the rice seized by the customs enforcement team during the search for smuggled rice in Shantou at Jiafa Shop on Deanhou Street, 25 bags belonged to merchants of that country, and demanded that we return them. After receiving this reply, the Shantou Municipal Government, considering that the fact that ronin had intercepted and robbed the customs enforcement ship and its cargo was clear, and should not be allowed to be denied, again cited various pieces of evidence on the 31st of last month to refute the consul of that country, demanding that the consul severely punish the ronin who caused the incident, return the robbed ship and cargo, apologize to us, and guarantee that the same incident would not happen again. As for the consul's request to return the foreign rice seized from Jiafa Shop belonging to merchants of that country, the municipal government, as it was unclear about the actual situation at the time, specially wrote to the Chao-Shan Customs Enforcement Office to investigate and reply for handling. Later, due to a three-day holiday for New Year's Day, government agencies and consulates only began to work on the 4th, and the two sides are still negotiating. It is reported that the Chao-Shan Customs Enforcement Office recently decided to arrest several local merchants in Chao-Shan who colluded with foreign smugglers, and sent a team to escort them to the province for punishment. At the same time, the stores of these traitors were sealed up, giving them the most severe punishment, in order to warn the stubborn. Therefore, the traitors who had previously had dealings with foreign smugglers were quite afraid and have changed their businesses to legitimate ones. However, foreign smugglers are still actively engaged in smuggling operations. Their cunning schemes involve changing the form of smuggled goods and disguising them as taxed goods, and then transporting them into the mainland for sale. It is reported that recently, many ronin have been found in the market buying old rice, bean, and hemp bags with tax stamps, because these hemp bags have tax stamps from the agricultural tax bureau, and can be used to pack smuggled goods, which can easily deceive people. In addition, some smuggle rice and beans by packing them in old wooden boxes or large porcelain jars to deceive inspectors. There are all kinds of tricks, nothing is too strange. Merchants from a certain country also fear losses, so recently they have personally escorted the smuggled goods transported from Shantou to the mainland to avoid being arrested. It is reported that the best-selling smuggled goods at present are broken rice. On the 6th and 7th of this month, a certain smuggling gang imported another batch of untaxed foreign rice, totaling more than 20,000 bags, from Southeast Asia. It is expected that they will use the above-mentioned disguise methods to sell them in Chao-Shan. It is reported that the Chao-Mei Agricultural Tax Bureau is paying close attention to this and plans to set up a proper method to prevent smuggled goods from being disguised as taxed goods. The customs enforcement office has also ordered close investigation to prevent leakage. (7th)

The Financial Crisis of Militaristic Japan (Part 2) 70

— Huang Fu

Regarding the increase in tax revenue, the estimated figures for next year are shown in Table 5 below:

Table 5 Estimated Tax Revenue for Next Year (Unit: 1,000 Yen)

(Increase/Decrease compared to this year) Income Tax 332,000 36,000 Land Tax 58,000 —— Business Profit Tax 62,000 11,000 Capital Interest Tax 15,000 —— Inheritance Tax 32,000 3,600 Liquor Tax 209,000 3,000 Sugar Consumption Tax 87,000 9,000 Textile Consumption Tax 42,000 9,000 Exchange Tax 14,000 1,600 Customs Duty 158,000 28,000 Stamp Revenue 79,000 2,500

(The above figures include 3 million yen from the revision of the Iron Manufacturing Promotion Law and 4 million yen from the revision of the Mineral Oil Tax – November 27, "Tokyo Asahi")

From the above figures, the most significant increases are in income tax and business profit tax, while the main decreases are in liquor tax, exchange tax, and stamp revenue. In this natural increase, we see that the increase in revenue is mainly from taxes based on assessment. In reality, stamp duty, liquor tax, exchange tax, etc., which increased due to the recovery of the economy, not only did not increase but decreased. Therefore, we can know that this kind of natural increase is not enough to indicate an improvement in the economic situation, but can only explain the improvement of tax collection technology and more stringent assessment. In addition, the increase in customs duties is not due to a turnaround in the economy, but to the revision of customs duty rates. (This fact can be seen from the fact that the increase in tonnage tax is not very large.) Therefore, the financial authorities believe that the so-called "natural" increase in financial improvement is essentially a disguised name for "coercive" increase. Because of coercion and manpower, its increase is also limited. Its rate of increase cannot keep pace with the rapidly increasing military expenditure, which is even more obvious.

Secondly, there is the assistance (accommodation) of special accounts. This is clearly just a temporary method used to alleviate the difficulty of budget compilation. According to the "Tokyo Asahi" on November 27, the amount of accommodation from special accounts that have never been diverted in the past is 12.5 million yen in next year's budget, including:

Table 6 Accommodation Amount of Special Accounts for Next Year (Unit: 1,000 Yen)

Managed by the Ministry of Railways (20% of the surplus of special accounts) 5,400

Managed by the Ministry of Colonial Affairs (10% of the surplus of special accounts in Korea, Taiwan, Karafuto, and the South Seas Agency) 5,000

Managed by the Ministry of Communications (20% of the surplus of the communication business special accounts) 2,100

Total 12,500

This kind of accommodation, in addition to showing the depletion of financial resources, clearly shows a plan to sacrifice colonial finance in order to share the deficit of the central general account. As for the third point, it is because the military's attitude is tough, and they had to admit the 20 million yen of resurrected demands. On the one hand, there is no way to find compensation from public bonds, and finally, the scattered financial resources are scraped together from various provinces - the so-called "cooperative budget of various provinces". Here, in addition to accommodating special accounts from the Ministries of Railways, Communications, and Colonial Affairs, they even fantastically ordered the Japan Iron Manufacturing Company, under the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, to increase dividends and allocate 2.8 million yen from the increased revenue from government shares. (The capital of Japan Iron Manufacturing is probably 159 million, of which 280 million are government shares, accounting for 80%. It is estimated that dividends will increase from 6% to 7%)!

From the above observations, we can know that the so-called gradual reduction of deficit bonds is only a slogan of temporarily muddling through using financial means, and on the other hand, it shows the extreme anxiety about the future of finance and the need for a universalization of financial technology caused by this anxiety.

In short, the extraordinary budget containing a huge amount of 1.05 billion in military expenditure has finally been compiled by piecing together. But what about the future? In response to the demands of financial capitalists, the deficit bonds have been reduced in appearance, but military expenditure is still expanding endlessly. Domestic financial resources have long been exhausted. Increasing taxes in general, using the increased burden on the poor to meet the demands of military expenditure, is no longer as simple as imagined. The progress of the proletarian parties in this year's local elections, and the qualitative and quantitative increase in labor disputes and tenant disputes in the past year, all indicate that Takahashi's statement that "natural disasters are constant, people's livelihoods are haggard, and there are many aspects of social policy worthy of consideration" is not just a concern. On the mainland, although adventurers have fortunately obtained a large piece of fat, regrettably there is no gastric juice in their own stomach to digest this fat and turn it into their own nourishment! Next year is the year of naval military expansion competition, so what will be used to satisfy this insatiable demand then?

The "gradual reduction of deficit bonds" completed by the "superhuman" efforts of the 82-year-old man has temporarily given the Japanese financial community a bit of heroic excitement and reassurance, but after this excitement cools down, the reassurance will quickly follow and also waver. The deficit bonds are gradually reduced, but the deficit in expenditure remains! So they began to stare at and worry about this permanent expansion of military expenditure. To overcome it, or to be overcome? In the point of gradual reduction of deficit bonds in next year's budget, the financiers overcame the military in appearance, but wasn't the military expenditure still increased by 38 million? In essence, it was still overcome. The comments in the "Tokyo Asahi" on December 1st and 2nd are extremely suggestive.

"The international situation in the Far East is now extremely clear in that Japan occupies a leading position. Since it already occupies the position of a leader, the regulation of the urgency of the international situation can, of course, be influenced by Japan to some extent. This is the basis for the possibility of granting a certain degree of flexibility to military expenditure. There are certainly absolute elements in military expenditure, but to regard all military expenditure as absolute and make the financial plan bow before it is a matter that the military authorities should also carefully consider." (1st: "Still a Confused Budget")

"Military expenditure of 1.05 billion yen accounts for 47% of the total budget. This is an increase of 38 million yen over this year. The demands of the General Staff Headquarters have been compromised, but if this is still not satisfactory, then how long will this trend continue? Just like what former Minister of the Army Araki said about the year in which the Manchurian Incident expenses will be normalized is something that the people cannot estimate. The lack of a fixed national policy on this expansion of military expenditure is really something that makes the people extremely uneasy.

"In this sense, the people who believe in the unclear state system also hope for the clarification of national defense and the establishment of a national policy on national defense. The cabinet members who cooperated in the budget cabinet should make greater efforts than piecing together financial resources, and should not be dragged along by the military. Everyone should work together to establish national policies in their own field, and at the same time, the military's autonomy should also take into account the strength of guiding the international situation, and give the people a prospect and reassurance regarding the future of military expenditure." (2nd: "The Future of Military Expenditure and the Establishment of National Policy")

Can this hope be realized? The attitude taken by the military recently and the facts mentioned above have all shown that the answer is pessimistic and uncertain. (Written in Kyoto on December 24, 1935)

Antung Sailing Ship Encountered Disaster at Sea; Adrift at Sea for More Than a Month; Ten Died of Starvation Out of Fifty-Nine 71

Qingdao Correspondence: The Public Security Sixth Branch of this city discovered a distressed sailing ship near Kaolao Island, Rongcheng yesterday. Because it had been drifting at sea for more than a month, ten of the fifty-nine crew members and passengers had starved to death. The details of the ship's disaster are recorded as follows:

Encountering Wind Mid-Journey: The ship was a large sailing ship from Antung named "Jin Zeng," ship number An Zi No. 1006, owned by Sun Shengqi, a native of Antung. The ship was chartered by people from Rizhao and Zhucheng counties to transport coffins to Rizhao County. The ship carried 107 sets of human bones, in addition to four coffins. There were a total of fifty-nine crew members and passengers. It departed from Antung on the seventh day of the eleventh month of the old calendar. After sailing for a day and a night, it suddenly encountered a hurricane. Both oars and rudder were lost, and it no longer had the ability to control itself. It could only drift in the turbulent waves and rely on fate.

Adrift for More Than a Month: After the ship drifted south with the wind, it drifted to the sea south of Korea. It was at sea for more than a month, unable to reach the shore. The food it carried was only enough for more than twenty days. When the food ran out, and the weather was cold and there were no clothes to keep warm, ten people died one after another due to hunger and cold. The remaining people knelt on the ship to pray, or knelt before the spirits and wept, asking the gods to protect them. In despair, they could only sit and wait for death.

Drifting to Qingdao: As it turned out, there is always a way out. Six or seven days ago, a strong east wind suddenly blew on the sea, and the ship drifted westward with the wind. At that time, all the boatmen were overjoyed. After five days and nights of struggle, it sailed to Kaolao Island near Rongcheng and was able to reach the shore. Statistics show that it had been drifting in the water for more than thirty days. In addition to the dead, there were still forty-nine survivors. Surviving from death can be said to be fortunate.

Authorities Provide Relief: After the ship arrived at Kaolao Island, it landed ashore and went to the police station of the Public Security Sixth Branch in Laoshan to report the disaster. The police station immediately reported the situation to the Public Security Bureau and asked for instructions on how to deal with it. After receiving the report, the bureau ordered the Sixth Branch to first prepare food for the passengers and boatmen, and then raise funds to send the passengers back to their original hometowns.

Shandong Provincial Department of Finance Encourages Silver Shops to Make Loans to Rescue All Industries in Jinan; Loan Amount 1.5 Million 72

Jinan Correspondence: This year, Shandong's native products have been in decline, and the sales of silk and flowers are also poor. Grain stores and native product stores, which operate in fresh rice and fresh fruit, suffered heavy losses last summer due to the impact of a sharp decline in prices. When the largest cotton warehouse, Dongxing Huahang, went bankrupt, it owed the market 80,000 to 90,000 yuan, resulting in Jinan's facade of strength hiding a fragile core for several years, which has reached a critical point. In addition, due to the impact of the situation, various banks have adopted a tightening policy on lending. Not only are new loans not being made, but old loans are being pressed for repayment. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly requested the Department of Finance to order various banks to continue lending to maintain the situation. Otherwise, half of the city's shops will face the risk of bankruptcy during the lunar New Year. The Department of Finance consulted with various banks, and the banks agreed to jointly contribute 2 million yuan with the money shops to form a loan committee. However, after asking the various head offices for instructions, the head offices ordered that borrowers must borrow from the banks through the Provincial Bank, and the amount was reduced to 1.5 million yuan. However, the Chamber of Commerce did not accept this method and still requested the Department of Finance to handle the matter as previously discussed. The Department of Finance believed that the various banks and silver shops were in Jinan and were interdependent and could not shirk responsibility. It drafted various loan methods and methods for disposing of collateral to ensure the safety of the capital of the lenders, submitted them to the provincial government for approval, and ordered various banks and money shops to handle the matter according to the previous plan. Although the Gregorian New Year has passed recently, the Lunar New Year is approaching, and various shops are busy soliciting overdue debts, and the market is experiencing extremely tight credit, which is causing great difficulty. At times of dispute, those with property and goods have nowhere to borrow. Of those who have the ability to repay, only two or three out of ten. If there is no further relief, there will be many who cannot support themselves and declare bankruptcy. Therefore, on the morning of the 10th, the Department of Finance convened a meeting of the Bank of China, Central Bank, Communications Bank, Minsheng Bank, and other banks, as well as the Silver Industry Association. Although the Donglai Bank, Shiye Bank, Continental Bank, and Shanghai Bank stated that they would not participate in the loan group, they were also invited to join the meeting. After everyone arrived, Wang Xiangrong, the Director of the Department of Finance, did not attend due to other matters, and the First Section Chief Wang Zaolin and Secretary Director Weng Zhiquan attended, explaining the recent alarming situation of Jinan's commerce. If there is no relief method, it is bound to bring down many. Regarding the loan issue, the Chamber of Commerce and various industry associations will investigate, set full guarantees, and organize a loan review committee to review. The Department of Finance, fearing that the banks could not repay the loans to the borrowers and that difficulties would arise when disposing of the collateral, also drafted methods for disposing of the collateral, ensuring that the loan was extremely solid. The silver shops and banks are all in Jinan, weathering the storm together, and should help each other to tide over this difficult time. Although the various banks and silver shops were extremely touched, they had real difficulties and requested that the loan amount be reduced to 1.5 million yuan. It was decided that the Bank of China, Central Bank, Communications Bank, and Minsheng Bank would each contribute 250,000 yuan, and the Silver Industry Association would contribute 100,000 yuan, for a total of 1.1 million yuan, to be lent out first. If it is still insufficient, the Donglai Bank, Continental Bank, Shiye Bank, and Shanghai Bank will each contribute 100,000 yuan to meet the need. Regarding the collateral, movable property is still the principle, but if the collateral is goods that must be sold in the store and cannot be returned to the bank's warehouse, immovable property can be used as collateral. With the exception of the Minsheng Bank, which is a government bank with unavoidable responsibilities and does not need to ask for instructions, the other banks all said that they still need to telegraph the head office for instructions, detailing the needs of Jinan City and requesting approval, and must reply in the near future, so that the Chamber of Commerce can establish a loan committee and release the money before the Lunar New Year. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned, and the various banks immediately telegraphed the head office for instructions. A reply from the Department of Finance is expected in three to five days. The biggest crisis in commerce is expected to be overcome. (10th)

Shandong Province Plans to Build a Highway from Mengyin, Laiwu, and Fei Counties, but Due to Significant Funding Needs, the Decision is to Postpone the Project 73

Jinan Correspondence: Southern Shandong is mostly mountainous. The areas around Mengyin, Laiwu, and Fei counties are particularly difficult to traverse. It's not just the precarious mountain paths, but also the complex and winding rivers, causing great hardship for travelers. There's a saying in these two or three counties about "nine mountains, eighteen rivers, and seventy-two gullies," highlighting the difficulty of travel. In past years, banditry was rampant in the mountains, making military suppression challenging, and troop movements were often agonizing. Chairman Han personally inspected these counties and is well aware of the situation. He now plans to take advantage of this winter lull to start road construction. Previously, he instructed the Department of Construction to build a road from Laiwu through Mengyin to Fei County. The Department of Construction sent technician Xu Jingfang to thoroughly survey the route. According to his completed survey report, the road is a total of 335 li long. Besides borrowing the existing motor roads on the sections from Xintai to Mengyin and from Pingyizhen to Fei County, there are still 185 Chinese miles (li) that need to be built. The mountain ridges are undulating, and there are many rivers. The first phase of excavation, along the stone ridges, is estimated to cost 712,360 yuan. Paving 2,000 meters of stone road at Baima Pass would cost 30,000 yuan. The remaining earthwork would be handled by conscripting laborers from the counties. Once the first phase is completed, cars could pass. The second phase involves building 37 relatively large bridges and 114 smaller bridges, with a total cost of materials and labor estimated at 630,200 yuan. The Director of the Department of Construction, Zhang Honglie, has submitted this report to the provincial government for review and action. However, Shandong Province is still recovering from disasters, and the people are impoverished. This section of road, just over 180 li, would require over 1.3 million yuan, making it impossible to complete. The provincial government meeting on the 10th has resolved to postpone the project. (10th)

Songjiang: Robbery and Murder of Two Victims

At the home of farmer Qian Jingen, in the Gujiezizhen area of Youchebang, Fengjing, on the evening of the 7th, more than ten bandits suddenly appeared, broke in, and robbed. They demanded the hidden silver but were unsuccessful. The bandits then used grass ropes to strangle the victims, Qian Yugen and his wife, Mrs. Lu. When the victims still refused to reveal the location, they were strangled to death on the spot, their eyes bulging and mouths open, a horrifying sight. The bandits dispersed in a panic. The next day, the Second Sub-Bureau was notified for investigation and then reported it to the local court for inspection. It is learned that the Prosecutor's Office has dispatched a prosecutor to Fengjing for the inspection.

Suzhou: Abuse of Maid Case Continues Hearing Yesterday.

Miss Tan Huizhu from Guangdong, residing at No. 17 Deren Lane, Xingjia Muqiao Road, Shanghai, was sentenced to one year and six months in prison by the Shanghai District Court for abusing her maid. Tan appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, and the trial opened on December 18th of last year. The result was that the case required further investigation, and the court ordered Tan Huizhu to post a written bail of 1,000 yuan before being released. The 11th was the date for the continuation of the trial. The appellant, Tan Huizhu, the maid, Xuejuan, and the second landlord, Wang Kaichang, all reported in at 2:00 PM. At around 3:00 PM, Fang Wen, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division I, along with Judge Si Wen, opened the court for trial. First, according to Tan Huizhu's testimony, the scars on Xuejuan were from burns inflicted by a neighbor named Yadain. This happened on September 5th of last year. The judge asked why she said it was a sore when questioned by the Public Security Bureau before. She replied that she did not know at the time. The court then questioned the second landlord, Wang Kaichang, who stated that he worked at the Aikefa Foreign Firm, leaving in the morning and returning in the evening, so he had no knowledge of the matter. Then Xuejuan was questioned, and she testified that the scars were from burns inflicted by a neighbor named Yadain. The judge asked why she pointed out Tan Huizhu as the one who burned her when questioned by the police officer. She replied that this was not the case. At this point, the court adjourned to the deliberation chamber. The prosecutor then took the stand to present his arguments, and lawyer He Yunqing made a defense on behalf of Tan. The arguments concluded, and a date was set for judgment. Tan Huizhu remained on her original bail, and Xuejuan and Wang Kaichang were ordered to return home.

Jiading: A Large Number of Refugees Disturb the Western Countryside

On the 7th, hundreds of refugees from the Tianfu Temple area of Kunshan County entered the western border of this county. In Hongjia Village, Tangqiaobang, and other places southwest of Wangxian Bridge in the Fourth District, they broke into people's homes,抢劫米粮,拐鷄打鴨, and caused great disturbance. Wuxi: The Truth Behind the Dasongfen Bloodshed Case is Revealed

On the morning of the 5th, a murder case was discovered at Dasongfen Tomb outside the south gate of Xiyi. The deceased was named Lin Yusheng, and his wife, Chen Ada, was only seventeen years old but quite promiscuous, almost anyone could sleep with her. She had affairs with her husband's brothers, Lin A'er and Lin Hesheng. This time, after Jinsheng was killed, the diligent investigation by his friend Shen Yongmao and the detectives led to Chen Ada being suspected of murder and taken into custody by the County Public Security Bureau for questioning. Lin Hesheng, the deceased's brother, was also considered a prime suspect and was also taken into custody at the same time. Bloodstains were found on the corner of Lin Hesheng's cotton robe and on his shoe uppers, which were identical in color to the blood at the scene of the crime. Therefore, he was placed under strict surveillance. Later, based on a tip, Lin A'er, a cousin of the deceased, was suspected of being an accomplice. The county detective team, accompanied by Shen Yongmao, went to the countryside and arrested Lin A'er on the way to Liqiao. After being brought to the city, they were interrogated separately. According to their confessions, both Lin A'er and Lin Hesheng had affairs with Ada. Hesheng wanted to be husband and wife with Ada for a long time, so he conspired with A'er and bought a sugar cane peeling knife for 150 yuan at Chong'an Temple. On the evening of the tenth day of the lunar calendar, Hesheng, together with A'er and the deceased, Jinsheng, drank wine in a hotel outside the south gate. They first got Jinsheng drunk. When they walked to the vicinity of Zhangyuan Temple, Jinsheng fell into the river. The two helped him up and took off his wet cotton robe. By the time they reached Dasongfen Tomb, Jinsheng could no longer walk and sat on a dirt pile. Hesheng first used the knife to stab Jinsheng in the neck, and then A'er held Jinsheng down and stabbed him twice more. Seeing that he was dead, they threw the knife into the pond and fled to Qingqi's house to sleep. Chen Ada also confessed that she had affairs with a soldier, her cousin Lin Shengbao, and her husband's brother Lin Hesheng. Hesheng told her that he planned to kill Jinsheng and then take her as his wife. Thus, the truth of the case has been revealed. Chief Inspector Wang ordered them to be closely guarded and then transferred to the county court for trial.

Long-distance bus accident

Jiangzhen: People from Gaobao Come to the Province to Petition

The Qingyang long-distance bus No. 1208 of the Jiangsu Provincial Highway Administration, traveling from north to south at 2:00 PM on the 6th, passed through the Fengshen Temple Qigong Hall on the Yun Causeway outside the west gate of Gaoyou City. The terrain was dangerous. The driver of the bus, due to careless driving, overturned into the Grand Canal. There were about 30 passengers in the bus, all of whom fell into the water. Neighboring residents of that section of the canal rescued more than a dozen men and women, but eight people drowned, a tragic scene. This caused opposition from the citizens of Gaoyou, and the Standing Committee Member of the Baoying County Party Department, Ji Xiaonan, together with more than ten citizens from Gaoyou County, including Xia Yuhua, brought a petition to the province. They arrived in the province at 3:00 PM on the afternoon of the 10th and petitioned the Provincial Government and the Department of Construction. The petition is recorded as follows: "The Jiangbei Yangqing Highway allows buses to pass, and the Yangshao section temporarily uses small transport. The route starts from Qingjiang and ends at Shaobo, along the Grand Canal, a long embankment of more than 300 li. The rapid land transportation relies solely on buses. As for the lack of vehicles and crowded passengers, we will not dwell on that. However, in less than a month, tragedies have occurred one after another. One overturned in a culvert in Liujiabao, but fortunately, a wooden bridge blocked it, preventing a major disaster. Half a month ago, a pedestrian was crushed to death north of Jieshou. The most tragic was on the 6th of this month, when a southbound bus overturned at the Qigong Hall outside the west gate of Gaoyou, with 30 passengers, and only 7 survivors. Only eight corpses have been recovered, and the whereabouts of the others are unknown. Whether they are alive or dead, their families have no news. Who doesn't have parents who fear for their longevity? Who doesn't have children who rely on them? Even if they are not husband and wife, they are as respectful as friends. Who doesn't have brothers who are as close as limbs? How can the living bear this? We believe that highways should facilitate passengers, but now they have become instruments of murder, with life in danger and uncertainty. Thinking of this, we are filled with fear. The citizens live in Gaoshi, in the middle section of the highway, and what we see and hear is heartbreaking. Everyone has compassion, and we believe that Your Excellency cares deeply. Hearing of this tragedy, how can you not be saddened? How should we plan for safety and protect the lives of passengers to avoid future accidents? We respectfully request that Your Excellency convene representatives from each county along the route for open discussion, to determine how bus drivers should be strictly screened, how routes should be revised, and how funding should be统筹, with careful consideration to ensure safety. Developing transportation and eliminating dangers will not only benefit the passengers of our two counties, but will also bring life to ten thousand families. In addition to submitting this petition directly to the Provincial Government, we respectfully submit this document, hoping that Your Excellency will review and implement it. Respectfully presented to the Chairman of the Provincial Government, Chen, and the Director of the Department of Construction, Shen."

Local News

In Areas Lacking Legal Tender Circulation, the Use of Existing Currency is Temporarily Allowed for Commercial Transactions. Businesses Receiving Existing Currency Should Immediately Exchange it for Legal Tender. The Municipal Government Issued an Order Yesterday for All Subordinate Agencies to Comply. 74

The Municipal Government of this city issued an order to its subordinate agencies yesterday stating, "Approved by the Ministry of Finance Qi Qian telegram, it is currently the end of the lunar year, a time of major closures, and commercial transactions are frequent. From now until the end of the lunar year, in areas where legal tender circulates, payments should be made in legal tender. In areas lacking legal tender circulation, the use of existing currency is permitted for income and expenditures, to provide convenience and show consideration. However, businesses receiving existing currency should immediately send it to the nearest legal tender exchange agency to exchange it for legal tender. They must not hoard or conceal it, causing inconvenience. As for the military and police in various places, regarding people carrying existing currency to purchase goods, and business personnel carrying the existing currency they have received, if they are not collecting, transporting, or smuggling for profit, they should still handle it in accordance with the Ministry's Youwei Qian telegram regulations. In addition to sending separate telegrams, a special telegram is sent to request that you investigate and handle the matter accordingly, and all subordinate agencies should comply with this order."
