Rong Zongjing Contributes Suggestions for Revitalizing Agriculture and Industry, Promoting Wheat Fields and Cotton Fields. 76

According to the Central News Agency, the topic of President Jiang's speech on New Year's Day at the Central Broadcasting Station was "The National Way to Self-Help and Saving the Country." The program in the speech included the New Life Movement and the National Economic Construction Movement. The implementation requirements and methods of the National Economic Construction Movement included eight items. If these are done conscientiously, it is definitely an easy task. Shanghai industrial tycoon Rong Zongjing has some suggestions for the first item, revitalizing agriculture, and the fifth item, promoting industry. He presented them to President Jiang of the Executive Yuan and Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry. He said, "I have been engaged in the flour and textile industries for more than 30 years. Food and clothing are the basic needs of people's lives, and the raw materials for the flour and textile industries are all agricultural products. Therefore, the revitalization of agriculture is closely related to people's food and clothing. The wheat produced in our country each year is not enough for the mechanized flour mills in the country for half a year, and the Maoxin Fuxin Flour Mills that I founded need more than 10 million祖. When there is a shortage of wheat, to maintain the people's food and the livelihood of workers, we have to purchase foreign wheat to supply the mills. Our country has many places suitable for growing wheat. Instead of relying on others, why not produce enough for ourselves? We should promote wheat fields and plant them in time, so that the output will increase year by year, reaching 100 million担, so that there is no fear of supply falling short of demand. As for the cotton production in our country, the numbers have been increasing in the past ten years. Through active cotton planting, the output has increased to more than 11 million担, but last year there were only more than 8 million担. Our country has a population of 400 million, and cotton production must increase to 16 million担 to meet the needs of the textile industry and the people. Today, all countries are promoting cotton fields, such as Brazil in South America, which is also increasing its output. Our country has a vast territory and a large population. Without actively planting cotton again, we cannot revive the countryside. This is my opinion on revitalizing agriculture."

President Jiang said, "If industry cannot be developed, material civilization cannot progress, and economic life cannot be satisfactory. Therefore, in addition to vigorously promoting agriculture, forestry, and mining, the most important thing is to strive for the development of industry. The textile industry is the most important industry in our country. The United Kingdom has more than 40 million spindles, India has more than 9 million, the United States has more than 30 million, and Japan has been increasing its spindles year by year. In 1935, it had increased to 10,296,528 spindles. Our country has only 2.5 million spindles, and foreign-owned factories in China have more than 2 million. When new cotton is on the market, many of our country's 2.5 million spindles are still idle. For example, Shenxin No. 2 and No. 5 factories have been shut down for almost a year, and there is no way to find a way to resume production. However, considering the needs of 400 million people, spindles must be promoted. If it is limited by economic and environmental factors, at a minimum, the existing number of spindles should be maintained. If the original number of spindles cannot be maintained, economic aggression cannot be resisted. What is the purpose of developing industry? In my humble opinion, maintaining the current state of the yarn industry is better than reducing interest rates and facilitating transportation. Maintaining the current situation is the only way to seek progress. Otherwise, we are still in the budding stage of the textile industry. If we don't irrigate it and destroy it, there is still hope for survival? This is my opinion on promoting industry. People who run factories now are all downcast and have unspeakable pain. After reading President Jiang's speech, I unconsciously became excited. Speaking from the standpoint of a businessman, I said a few words about my own interests. I don't know if I am right. I still hope that the government and the public will teach me."

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Negotiations to Stop Japanese Residents from Issuing Paper Money, Which Will Cause Our Country's Newly Reorganized Currency System to Fail Completely and Fall Into a Chaotic Situation. 84

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting negotiations to stop Japanese residents from issuing paper money in Shanghai. The submission stated, "According to reports, Japanese residents in Shanghai have requested their country to circulate Japanese yen banknotes in Shanghai, with the number temporarily limited to 2 million yuan. All Japanese factories will use these banknotes to pay workers' salaries and purchase goods from Chinese people. It is also heard that Japan has already implemented the scheduled steps one by one. This is a further step compared to the previous rumors that it would only be used among Japanese residents. Although foreign banks in our country's commercial ports have issued banknotes, they have long been gradually withdrawn and are almost extinct. This precedent should not be reopened. Moreover, Japanese yen banknotes are said to be based on gold, which is very different from the banknotes issued by foreign merchants based on silver dollars. This measure is no different from applying the old trick of the gold standard implemented in Dalian to Shanghai, which will cause the achievements of our country's currency system, which has been reorganized in recent years, to fail completely and fall into a chaotic situation. Therefore, we respectfully request that Your Excellency (Ministry) review and approve the matter, and kindly order negotiations to stop it, and at the same time order the Central Bank to properly plan effective preventive measures to ensure complete success, which is extremely urgent."

Jiangda and Xinjiang Vessels Collide the Night Before Last, Both Damaged and Sent to Repair 85

The Taikoo Company's Xinjiang vessel, 2,646 tons, arrived in Shanghai from Qingdao and was docked at the company's No. 1 wharf on Xinkai River. It was originally scheduled to load cargo yesterday and sail to Shantou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou. At around 5 p.m. on the 10th, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Changjiang vessel Jiangda arrived and approached Xinkai River. As the ship's body reached the Jinliyuan Wharf, the acting captain and first mate, Xin Shaoqin, immediately turned the ship around there, preparing to berth at the wharf, and dropped anchor first. At this time, the Ningbo line vessels Xin Beijing and Xin Ningshao were coming up behind the Jiangda, causing the Jiangda vessel to reverse, unable to move backward, because reversing would cause a major disaster by colliding with Xin Ningshao. As a result, the bow of the Jiangda vessel collided with the Taikoo Xinjiang vessel. The bow of the Jiangda hit the stern of the Xinjiang, and both sides were damaged.

Damage Situation: The Xinjiang vessel is a sea-going vessel with extremely strong steel plates. The bow of the Jiangda vessel hit the right stern cabin of the Xinjiang vessel, damaging the seventh longitudinal stringer and bending the iron plate. As for the cement and wooden planks used to reinforce the bow of the Jiangda vessel, they were also completely destroyed. After the accident, the acting owner of the Jiangda, Zhe Shaoqin, went to the Xinjiang vessel to inspect the damage together. It was not until yesterday morning that the Maritime Affairs Bureau and the insurance company were notified, requesting technicians to inspect the damage so that repairs could be made at the shipyard.

Two Ships Enter the Shipyard: The Xinjiang vessel was originally scheduled to sail to Nanhua today, but since it was hit and damaged, after inspection by the insurance company and the Customs Port Affairs Office yesterday afternoon, it was sent to the Jiangnan Shipyard in the afternoon to enter the dock for repairs. It will take more than a day or two to complete the work. The company has reassigned another ship to replace it on the Nanhua run. The Jiangda vessel was also inspected yesterday afternoon and is scheduled to enter the shipyard for repairs today. It will take at least four or five days to complete the repairs.

Shipowner's Report: Xin Shaoqin, the acting owner of the Jiangda, reported to the General Office yesterday, saying that the Jiangda vessel dropped anchor and turned around to berth at the wharf due to wind direction and tidal conditions, causing a collision with the Xinjiang vessel. He stated that at 3:04 p.m. on the 10th, the Jiangda vessel entered the Wusong Estuary. After the ship passed the Meifu Petroleum Depot, it slowed down. When it reached Lujiazui, it changed to allow the green light to pass, waiting for the Xin Beijing vessel to exit. When it arrived at the Taikoo Wharf, it discovered a tugboat exiting from the alley. Because the Suiyang vessel was berthed at the buoy in that port, and the Xinjiang vessel was also docked at the Xinkai River Taikoo High Wharf, the vessel took the middle alley forward. When it passed the Suiyang, it stopped at 5:05 p.m., close to the stern of the ship, turned to the starboard and dropped anchor, quickly reversing, intending to berth at the Xinkai River China Merchants Wharf. However, at that time, the northeast wind was rising, and although the anchor was dropped and the car was reversed, it had little effect, and the bow of the ship drifted toward the Xinjiang vessel. At the same time, the Xin Ningshao vessel was sailing past the stern of the vessel. During the turning, it collided with the Xinjiang vessel. Subsequently, the vessel berthed at the wharf. He and the first and second mates immediately boarded the Xinjiang vessel to inspect and saw that the seventh transverse stringer was damaged. The bow of the vessel was also damaged. Therefore, the circumstances were reported. (The following is omitted.)

The Changjiang Six Vessels Distribute Water Transport Expenses Proportionately, Continued Handling After Expiration, Contract Terms Slightly Revised 86

Due to the scarcity of cargo transportation on the Changjiang River last year, the six shipping companies, including Nissin and Ningshao, repeatedly lowered water transport prices, competing to take on cargo. This not only sharply reduced revenue but also affected the survival of the entire shipping industry. Therefore, in July, they jointly convened a meeting to standardize water transport prices and implement a proportional distribution system, hiring Thomson Accountants as consultants and setting up an office at No. 2 Guangdong Road. The initial contract was signed for a trial period of six months, which will expire at the end of this month. The reporter inquired there yesterday and learned that since the implementation of proportional distribution of water transport expenses, the results have been good. After the expiration, in addition to slightly revising the terms of the original contract, the decision was made to continue handling it. It is reported that the validity period is still six months, and each shipping company may not withdraw midway until the expiration.

In addition to negotiating with the Money Trade Joint Reserve to collect money shop bills on its behalf, it has also added entrusted agency exchange notices, and business will continue as usual on Sundays. Entrusted Agency: The Bank Joint Reserve Committee's clearing position is full and no additional desks can be added. It is specifically stipulated that any member bank of the industry association that is unable to join as a clearing bank due to the limited space in the clearing house may entrust the association to act as its clearing agent. Currently, there are a total of thirty-eight clearing houses. Business as Usual on Sundays: The clearing house's notice reads, in brief, that the industry association, upon the recommendation of the association, has already stipulated that from this year onwards, all branches of each bank in the city will be closed all day on Sundays. The chaotic habits have been transformed into a neat and uniform new regulation, which is a deeply gratifying event this year. However, at present, the money trade industry has not been able to implement this uniformly. Therefore, the association's collection of bills on Sundays must still be handled as usual.

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Strictly Prohibits Smoking and Intensifies Investigation and Arrest Work, Many Opium Dens and Smokers Have Been Cracked Down on in Recent Days, The Drug Rehabilitation Hospital Has Increased Bed Capacity to Accommodate 93

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, after the registration of smokers ended at the end of last year, began this year to compile a register and classify statistics, and the work of investigating and arresting smokers is becoming increasingly tense. In the past ten days, many opium dens and smokers have been cracked down on. The number of people in the existing drug rehabilitation hospital has increased sharply, and special beds have been added to accommodate them. The details are recorded as follows.

Total Number of Registered Smokers Announced

The Public Security Bureau announced yesterday that the total number of registered smokers from July 1 to the end of December was 30,634, including 12,686 with ordinary licenses, 17,940 with poor people's licenses, and 8 with travel licenses, collecting a total of 74,218 yuan in license fees. In addition, 4,041 people were unable to obtain licenses and applied for abstinence, and 2,873 people had been discharged from the hospital after abstinence. The statistical breakdown of smokers' ages, occupations, and addresses is currently being compiled. Smokers' ages are mostly between 45 and 55, occupations are mostly coolies, and addresses are mostly in the Lao Beimen Yimiao area. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau Water Patrol Team announced that a total of 6,207 households had guaranteed that there were no smoking boat crews.

Opium Dens and Smokers: Many Cracked Down On

Since the bureau's investigation and arrest unit adopted the method of rewarding informers and joint investigations, the land and water investigations and arrests have become increasingly tense. The bureau's detective team and the police officers of the smoker registration section have been dispatched day and night, and in recent days, they have arrested more than 800 male and female smokers. About 90 private opium dens have also been cracked down on. Lao Beimen, Xin Zha, Shiliupu, Yimiao, Hengfeng Road, Menggu Road, and Ximen Branches have all made breakthroughs. In addition, the bureau recently found a recidivist smoker, Bao Zuojun, at No. 24 Hongyun Lane, Yuezhou Road, who had been rehabilitated by the bureau. He was ordered to rehabilitate again and was sent to the Songhu Garrison Command for strict legal action yesterday afternoon.

Drug Rehabilitation Hospital: Increased Bed Capacity

The Municipal Central Drug Rehabilitation Hospital, which was jointly planned by the Public Security Bureau and the Health Bureau, cannot be established immediately due to funding and layout reasons. However, on the Public Security Bureau's side, the drug rehabilitation work cannot be delayed due to the congestion of drug addicts and those waiting to be sent to the hospital for abstinence. Therefore, it was decided to add beds and use double-layer beds in the existing North and South Municipal Drug Rehabilitation Hospitals, the Drug Rehabilitation Hospital for Criminals in Caohejing, and the Longhua Drug Rehabilitation Center. The original number of beds in Shanghai South was 100, which has been increased to 180. The original number of beds in Shanghai North was 250, which has been increased to 500. The original number of beds in the Criminal Drug Rehabilitation Center was 100, which has been increased to 200. The original number of beds in the Provisional Drug Rehabilitation Center was 100, which has been increased to 200. Currently, the total number of beds in each hospital has been increased to 1,080, which is temporarily enough to accommodate them.

Drug Rehabilitation Hospital: Strictly Limited Fees

The city's anti-smoking authorities, in order to limit the excessive fees charged by temporary drug rehabilitation hospitals, have specially formulated measures for the management and designation of hospitals to undertake temporary drug rehabilitation work in the city, strictly limiting and regulating the fees. It is now known that this has been approved by the Municipal Government's instructions. The fees charged by each hospital for drug rehabilitation patients are as follows: (A) First-class ward, 4 to 6 yuan per person per day, including meals and medical expenses; (B) Second-class ward, 2 to 3 yuan per person per day, including meals and medical expenses; (C) Third-class ward, a total of 1 yuan per day, including meals and medical expenses; (D) All injectable drugs and supplements may be discussed with the drug rehabilitation patients by each hospital separately and charged separately. Drug rehabilitation patients must be hospitalized for abstinence and may not be discharged freely. The Municipal Public Security and Health Bureaus may, at any time, transfer people who have been rehabilitated by each hospital to the Municipal Drug Rehabilitation Agency for verification.

Anti-Smoking Committee: Compiles and Prints Special Publication

The Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, with the completion of smoker registration, the anti-smoking work can be declared to have come to an end. A special publication on anti-smoking has been compiled, which compiles various materials. In addition to photos of Chairman Chiang, Mayor Wu, and members of the committee, the text includes Wang Xiaolai's publication preface, Du Yuesheng's "The Anti-Smoking Problem in Shanghai," Cai Bubai's "My Views on Anti-Smoking," Deng Qingshan's "The Principles of Opium Addiction and Anti-Smoking Methods," as well as the various anti-smoking and anti-drug laws and regulations promulgated by the Military Affairs Committee's headquarters, and the committee's anti-smoking efforts. It is quite complete and will be distributed to all sectors of society to facilitate anti-smoking propaganda.

Traditional Chinese Medicine Doctors Have No Right to Extract Teeth, Luo Xiangfu Practices What He is Not Qualified For, Huang Genquan Asks for Good Teeth 98

Luo Xiangfu, 40 years old, from Yancheng, is a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner, lives in Pudong, and once had a traditional Chinese medicine license issued by the Municipal Health Bureau. Since he held the kettle, no one cared about him, so he was down on his luck. Recently, he had a whimsical idea and set up a dentist stall at the Yuhang Bridge embankment in the city without authorization, using the traditional Chinese medicine license to deceive people and extract teeth for treatment. A few days ago, Huang Genquan, a resident of Hai, who runs an ocean iron shop at No. 111 Laobaidu Street, (27 years old) sought Luo for treatment because of toothache. Luo said that the painful tooth must be extracted and stated that it would cost 40 cents. Unexpectedly, the pain became more severe after the extraction. He immediately went home to sleep. When he looked in the mirror yesterday, he unexpectedly found that the extracted tooth was a good tooth. So he was extremely angry and ran to Luo to negotiate, demanding the return of the extraction fee and compensation for the good tooth. Luo refused, resulting in an argument. The beat police Liu Fangqiu arrived and took him to the Yimiao Police Station. After questioning, Liu So feared that Luo Xiangfu had a traditional Chinese medicine license, not a dentist, and should not extract teeth for others. Divine Shoal Dredging Project Scheduled for Completion in Five Years; Beacon Installation to Commence Night Work Immediately; Another Dredger to Be Built; Construction Ship's Superintendent to Be Replaced Upon Completion of Term 101

According to a Datong News Agency reporter's continued inquiries with the Whangpoo Conservancy Board regarding the dredging of the Divine Shoal outside the Wusong Estuary, night and day dredging will soon commence. Simultaneously, the large dredger designed by the Board will be put out for bids for construction, with a deadline of one and a half years for completion, to facilitate the Divine Shoal dredging project. Details are as follows:

Glimpses of the Dredging Work

The Divine Shoal is located approximately thirty English miles northeast of the Wusong Estuary, at the center of the Yangtze River estuary, a vital navigational route. Since the arrival in Shanghai of the "Construction" dredger, ordered from Germany in April of last year, it has been dredging the shoal. The planned initial dredging program covers an area 20 miles long and 1,000 feet wide, deepening the water from 15 feet at low tide to 21.5 feet, removing approximately 20 million tons of soil. Currently, sections such as the Lanjiang Shoal have been initially dredged, with approximately 700,000 tons of soil removed from the dredging area. Including soil removed outside the designated area, the total exceeds one million tons.

Change of Ship's Superintendent

To accelerate the dredging work, the Board will soon initiate night work. However, the dredging area is a busy waterway, and to prevent collisions and other dangers, they are currently consulting with the Customs Maritime Department to install long-range floating beacon lights. Night work will commence once these beacon lights are installed. Simultaneously, the Board's dredging plan is scheduled for five years, requiring two large dredgers. Therefore, the construction of another dredger is urgent. The Chief Engineer has completed the design, and bids for construction will be solicited soon. Furthermore, it is understood that the superintendent of the "Construction" dredger, an experienced professional, was dispatched by the German Schichau shipyard. However, his term is only one year, which has now expired. The Board is currently searching for a suitable replacement.

Xu Yizeng Sues Traditional Chinese Medicine Doctor; Fetus Presented in Court; "I Mistook Pregnancy for Amenorrhea"; Contents of Alcohol Bottle to Be Evaluated 102

Xu Yizeng, age 31, a local native and manager of the Hongyun Photography Studio at 82 Pintang Lane, Nanjing Road, whose wife, Ms. Zhu, was approximately four months pregnant, felt unwell and went to see Yu Zuotang, an expert in gynecology practicing traditional Chinese medicine at 72 Guanbao Lane, Xiangfen Lane, Nanjing Road, on November 19th of last year. After examination, Yu diagnosed her with amenorrhea, not pregnancy, and prescribed medication to promote menstruation. The prescription consisted entirely of surface-acting remedies. However, after Ms. Zhu took the medicine, her condition not only failed to improve but worsened. She returned for a follow-up consultation on the 22nd, but Yu insisted it was amenorrhea and prescribed medicine to regulate the surface. Ms. Zhu took it as prescribed. Unexpectedly, after taking the medicine, she experienced severe abdominal pain and heavy bleeding, leading to unconsciousness and the miscarriage of the four-month-old fetus. She was rushed to another doctor, who diagnosed the error made by Yu Zuotang. Therefore, the miscarried fetus was preserved in alcohol to prevent decay. She then engaged lawyers Shen Zongyong and Wang Shouan to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, accusing Yu Zuotang of abortion and requesting that he be punished under Article 291, Section 1 of the Criminal Code and ordered to pay substantial damages. After an initial hearing by the First Special District Court, a continued hearing was held yesterday afternoon in the Second Criminal Court by Judge Jiang Shuzi. Xu Yizeng presented the fetus, preserved in an alcohol-filled bottle, to the court, while Yu engaged lawyer Xiao Zhuanding for his defense. The plaintiff's lawyer, to ensure fairness, requested the court to submit the fetus for expert evaluation. Judge Jiang instructed Xu Nengwu to pay ten yuan for the evaluation fee. Xu agreed to pay. The court then adjourned the hearing pending the results of the evaluation.

Yao Yunqi Suspiciously Discards Paper Package Full of New Banknotes; Previous Case in 1931; Received Ten Dollars for Carrying a Small Package 104

Qian Chenglong, a detective inspector, Zhou Bingcheng, a scout, and Greulich (transliteration), a Western detective inspector, along with detectives Li Liansheng and Le Sixiang, were patrolling Pingji Li Road at noon on the 10th when they spotted a suspicious-looking man between Lafayette Road and Boer Road. The man was carrying a paper package. Upon seeing the detectives approaching, he threw the package on the ground and fled. The detectives picked up the package, opened it, and found it full of new banknotes. They immediately gave chase and apprehended the man at the intersection of Lafayette Road and Annakin Road. They brought him back to the police station, where they examined the banknotes in detail and found them to be counterfeit one-yuan notes of the old version issued by the Bank of China, totaling eight hundred yuan. The man identified himself as Yao Yunqi, 28 years old, from Nanhui, Pudong, a coppersmith residing at No. 16 Shipipi Lane in the city. He stated that a woman on Pingji Li Road had given him the banknotes to deliver, and that the woman was following him but escaped when he was arrested. Yesterday morning, the police sent Yao, along with the counterfeit banknotes, to the Second Special District Court for questioning. Judge Li Changnian and Clerk Wang Baoxun conducted the preliminary hearing in the First Criminal Court at 11:00 AM. Gu Shouxi, the lawyer from the Police Department, described the arrest and stated that the police had discovered that the defendant was previously arrested on September 10, 1931, also for counterfeiting banknotes. However, the court found insufficient evidence and acquitted him. Because the Police Department still needed to investigate the case in detail and apprehend the accomplices who were still at large, they requested an extension of one week to detain the defendant while the case was investigated. The lawyer submitted the counterfeit banknotes as evidence. Yao Yunqi testified that around 10:00 PM on the 9th of this month, an acquaintance, Qian Zhixiang, told him to go to the Yuanyuan Teahouse at No. 148 Boer Road the next morning for tea. When he arrived at the teahouse on time, he met Qian and his friend Jin Yusheng. They told him that Jin's wife had a package of "fancy paper" that she wanted him to deliver to a guest at the Nanyang Restaurant on Boer Road and that he would be paid ten yuan. He went downstairs, walked north along Pingji Li Road, and about thirty storefronts down, a woman approached him and gave him the package. The woman followed behind him, and when he was arrested, she escaped. He claimed he did not know the package contained counterfeit banknotes. The court reviewed the testimony, adjourned the hearing to 10:00 AM on the 18th, and remanded the defendant in custody.

Implementation of Concession's Ban on Opium and Drugs Awaits Translation of Regulations into English for Foreign Police Officers 105

The First Special District Court, in adjudicating opium and drug cases, should follow the Ministry of Justice's directive and abide by the anti-drug and anti-opium regulations promulgated by the Superintendent-General for the Suppression of Opium. However, due to the unique circumstances of the concessions, this has not yet been implemented. Recently, after discussions between President Guo Yuntao of the court and the Public Works Department, it was originally decided that, starting from the 11th of this month, all opium and drug cases apprehended by the various police stations would be prosecuted by the Public Works Department in accordance with the anti-drug and anti-opium regulations. However, after receiving the court's notification, the Public Works Department realized that the regulations were written entirely in Chinese, which the foreign police officers in the various police stations did not understand. Therefore, it was difficult to apply them immediately. The regulations now need to be translated into English so that the foreign police officers can thoroughly understand the text before they can be invoked in cases to avoid discrepancies. Therefore, a considerable period of time is required to make the necessary arrangements, and the original implementation date of the 11th has had to be postponed.

Zhang Wu vs. Xie Lianqing: Litigation Arises Over Management of Estate 106

Accountant's Audit Reveals Discrepancies; Judge Instructs Defendant's Lawyer to Take Responsibility

Zhang Wu, a woman from Ningbo, residing at No. 2 Tangshan Road, engaged lawyers Xiang Xun and Peng Yuanxun in December of last year to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Division of the District Court, accusing Xie Lianqing, from Zhenhai, Ningbo, residing at No. 1 Qinganfang, Guangqi Road, of intentional misappropriation of estate funds under her management, requesting a legal investigation to uphold justice, along with a private prosecution. The lawsuit stated that her late husband, Yan Zhong, unfortunately passed away in September 1926 due to illness. Because the plaintiff's sons were still minors, the Zhang Xiafang Estate Management Committee was organized by fellow villagers and friends, with the defendant Xie Lianqing serving as an executive member, stationed at the Hengchangxiang Clock and Machine Shipbuilding Factory founded by the deceased husband. All of the deceased husband's assets were under the defendant's control. Last year, the plaintiff, seeing that the various businesses were facing financial difficulties, entrusted accountant Huang Bingzhang to audit the accounts. The plaintiff discovered that the defendant had intentionally enriched herself at the expense of others, taking advantage of her position as estate manager to sell the real estate on the Bund without authorization. According to the accountant's report, there was a discrepancy of 64,266.66 taels of silver, and evidence of breaches of trust and misappropriation was numerous. The defendant was indeed guilty and had no defense. The plaintiff requested a thorough investigation. The court accepted the lawsuit and ordered a preliminary hearing, resulting in the defendant Xie Lianqing being released on bail pending further instructions. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Chen Jingyi specially opened the 12th courtroom for a continued hearing. The plaintiff Zhang Wu, accompanied by lawyers Xiang and Peng, appeared in court. The defendant Xie Lianqing also engaged lawyer Wang Luqing to defend her. Lawyer Peng stated that the accountant Huang Bingzhang, who was summoned to testify, had gone to Hangzhou Electric Power Company to audit accounts on the 4th of this month, and would return to Shanghai in a few days. He requested the court to postpone the hearing. The defendant's lawyer also requested that the court summon four witnesses, including Dong Xingsheng, to protect the defendant's legal interests. The judge, after reviewing the arguments, instructed the defendant's lawyer: "The defendant must bear a certain responsibility in this case. The criminal charges cannot be withdrawn. However, regarding the civil aspects, it is permissible to seek a settlement with the plaintiff outside the court." The court granted a postponement for a consolidated hearing. Xie Lianqing remained released on the original bail, and because the guarantor was not present, lawyer Wang was responsible for ensuring her release.

Rickshaw Pullers in the Special District Resume Work After Strike; Zhang Dengying's Condition Improving 107

Rickshaw pullers in Shanghai's Special District, after a clash with the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, which led to the arrest of some pullers and sparked a strike by a portion of the pullers, resumed work yesterday, according to sources from the Rickshaw Industry Guild. Some of the arrested pullers have been handed over to the court and will be resolved through legal channels. The rest of the striking pullers resumed work yesterday. No unfortunate incidents occurred yesterday, and order was maintained. According to sources from the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association, the Association's Director-General Zhang Dengying, who was assaulted by rickshaw pullers the day before, is now recuperating in a hospital in the International Settlement and is in good condition.

Loan Request Denied, Assailant Slashes with Five Axes; Wan Fuquan Firmly Refuses; Huang Quanrong Gathers Gang for Assault 109

Wan Fuquan, a 26-year-old native of Wuxi, residing at No. 452, the intersection of Huishan Road and Jingzhou Road in Pudong, had a fellow villager and friend named Huang Quanrong who had previously asked Wan for a loan but was refused. Huang harbored a grudge. Around 7:00 PM last night, Wan was having dinner at home when Huang knocked on the door and entered, asking to borrow ten yuan. Wan firmly refused. A quarrel erupted. At that moment, over ten strong men crowded into the doorway, each wielding an axe. They knocked Wan to the ground and slashed him with three axes on his right leg and two axes on his left leg, causing him to bleed profusely. Seeing the damage they had caused, the assailants fled. Neighbors followed and apprehended one of the accomplices, who was handed over to the police for investigation. The injured man was rushed to the Sacred Heart Hospital by police ambulance for treatment.

Zhang Xu, a young woman from Nanxun, due to her husband's poverty and illness, voluntarily went to a job placement agency near Baxianqiao in September of last year to seek employment as a servant. The owner of the agency, seeing her youth and vulnerability, colluded with Xu Wang, a pimp at No. 42 Nanjing Road, and Li Meili, at No. 6 Le Yu Li, to sell the woman to Qiu Yongnian, a pimp at No. 10 Huile Li, Yunnan Road, for prostitution. When the police went to Qiu Yongnian's home to investigate, Qiu's four prostitutes, known as Lao Qi, Lao Ba, Da Nv, and Qiao Yun, had also fled. It was suspected that Xu Wang had forewarned them. Eurasia's Third Jumbo Jet Returns to Shanghai Last Night; Carries Nine Passengers from Baotou, Chengdu, and Other Locations; Renowned German Pilot Returns to Shanghai After Inspection 111

Eurasia Aviation Corporation's second Junkers Ju 52 jumbo jet, which flew from Shanghai to Chengdu last Wednesday for the inaugural test flight of the Shaanxi-Chengdu route, with renowned German aviator Herr Krog personally piloting the aircraft at the company's request to inspect various stations along the Eurasia Shanghai-Xinjiang-Shaanxi-Chengdu routes, arrived safely at Longhua at 8:15 PM last night, according to a report from the East China News Agency reporter who contacted the company. The aircraft carried nine passengers from Chengdu, Baotou, Xi'an, Zhengzhou, Nanjing, and other locations, as well as one bag of airmail from various locations. Herr Krog, the renowned German aviator who accompanied the aircraft to inspect the Eurasia stations, also returned to Shanghai yesterday after completing his mission. Herr Krog is currently drafting an inspection report, which he will submit to General Manager Li for review tomorrow to facilitate improvements. The inaugural test flight of the Shaanxi-Chengdu route was reportedly very successful. Additionally, Second Pilot Do Xu, who piloted the third jumbo jet to China, along with wireless operator Boble and mechanic Kroji, who served on the aircraft, departed for Germany aboard the British company's "Cathay" mail ship a few days ago.

Restaurant Industry Requests Postponement of Aviation Donation Levy 112

The restaurant industry sent a letter to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce stating: "We respectfully inform you that our members, including Tian Hongyun Restaurant and others, have reported that the restaurant business in the city is sluggish, with most operating at a loss and barely managing to survive. Moreover, all restaurants have been affected by the group weddings organized by the city government. Regarding the collection of aviation donations, at a meeting convened on April 30, 1935, by the Shanghai Recruiting Team of the China Aviation Association, our chairman, representing the industry, expressed the opinion that due to the poor economic climate, the implementation should be postponed. Furthermore, we discovered that the China Aviation Association did not notify our association of the meeting convened for the restaurant industry. Since the publication of the news that the aviation donation would be levied starting January 15, 1936, members have been inquiring and feel helpless. Although it is collected from customers, it inevitably affects our business. Therefore, we respectfully request that your chamber review the situation and forward this letter to the head office of the Shanghai Recruiting Team of the China Aviation Association, taking into account the difficulties of businesses and postponing the levy to ease public sentiment and show compassion. We sincerely appreciate your cooperation."

French Concession: Reactions to the Levy of Donations for Lights and Signs - Lao Qing He Silver Store Implements Power Outage - Municipal Federation Sends Letter to Taxpayers' Association for Negotiation 113

The Second Special District Citizens' United Association, First District Branch, regarding the matter of the Lao Qing He Silver Store on Bubbling Well Road being cut off from electricity by the French Municipal Council for levying donations for lights and signs, sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession yesterday, requesting negotiation. The original letter is excerpted as follows: Respected Sirs,

According to a letter from our member store, Lao Qing He Silver Store, located at 152 Bubbling Well Road, stating that on January 3rd of this year, they received a letter from the French Municipal Council, translated as saying, "We hereby notify you that your store must pay the light and sign donation of forty-two yuan for 1935 before December 31st, otherwise water and electricity will be cut off, (Note) the store was established more than twenty years ago, and has been installed for two years, without any notice of donation. Now the Municipal Council is extremely distressed by this commercial disruption, which cannot be afforded. They were preparing to present reasons and request the bureau to negotiate, but suddenly on the 9th of this month, the electricity was cut off, resulting in darkness and inability to do business. Therefore, they request your association to provide prompt relief, that is, to increase donations and taxes, and especially to use unreasonable power outages as a means of coercion, which is a great loss of the original intention of maintaining commerce. According to the previous situation in the letter, it is reasonable to send a letter to your association, preside over justice, and seriously negotiate with the French Municipal Council to restore the electricity of the store, and to argue with reason against the exorbitant donations, to achieve the purpose of canceling the donations, to appease merchants and people, and to avoid public dissatisfaction.

National Physicians' Federation, Fourth National Congress of Delegates 119

The Fourth National Congress of Delegates of the National Physicians' Federation was held at the Xuan Palace Hotel in Hankou starting on January 1st of this year. Representatives from Yunnan, Guangxi, Chongqing, Ganxian, Peiping, Hunan, Qingdao, Anqing, Wuhu, Nanjing, Shanghai, Rugao, Jinsha, Hangzhou, Jiangyin, Zhenjiang, Yongjia, Shenyang, Gansu, and other places, as well as representatives from the Hankou Hubei Provincial Physicians' Association, totaling more than 300 people, attended. The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM on New Year's Day. Representatives from the local Party Department, the Health Department, the Provincial Government, the Municipal Government, the Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the National Lawyers' Association, and the local Lawyers' Association all attended and delivered speeches. A preparatory meeting was held at 11:00 AM to pass the rules of procedure, and Xu Naili, Cai Yumen, Chen Fangzhi, Hu Dingan, Di Huasan, Shen Zhongling, Xu Zuyi, Yang Boru, Chuai Yiran, Zhang Dongting, and Zhang Senyu were elected as the presidium of eleven members, and a review committee was organized to review the proposals in groups. The members of the medical administration group were Dai Xiamin, Zhao Jisheng, Zhang Ding, Min Jianhui, Shao Jiyun, Jiang Huchen, and You Zhiyong, totaling seven people, convened by Dai Xiamin. The members of the compilation group were Yang Yusheng, Zhou Zhenyun, Chen Weitang, Li Ziheng, and Zhang Shibin, totaling five people, convened by Yang Yusheng. The members of the suggestion group were Jiang Zhenxun, Cheng Hanzhang, Hu Jingou, Zhu Hongzhi, Wen Yiqi, Lu Yongchun, and Chi Zhongjiu, totaling seven people, convened by Jiang Zhenxun. The members of the conference affairs group were Zhou Mingyu, Gu Nankui, Hao Juemin, Ling Chaoqun, and Shi Ruxiong, totaling five people, convened by Zhou Mingyu. At noon, a public banquet was held by the Hubei Provincial Physicians' Association and the Hankou Municipal Physicians' Association. The first formal meeting was held in the afternoon to pass the draft of the Physicians' Association Law and submit it to the government for adoption, and the proposal for the establishment of a health cooperative, which had been discussed at the previous congress, was re-discussed and resolved to be submitted to the government for promotion. The meeting adjourned at 6:30 PM. In the evening, a public banquet was held by the New Asia, Xinyi, and Wuzhou Three Pharmaceutical Factories. At 9:00 AM on the second morning, the second formal meeting was held to pass a total of eleven proposals from the medical administration group on construction, crackdown, and protection issues, and a total of nine proposals from the suggestion group on the physician law, forensic medicine, and hygiene, including the proposal to petition the government to promote eugenics to strengthen the nation, and the proposal that all localities should promote occupational hygiene guidance, which are particularly important for the future of the nation. At noon, Mr. Yang Yongtai, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, hosted a banquet at the Provincial Government Auditorium. Mr. Yang delivered a speech on the spot, mainly in three points: 1. The new medicine is based on the imperial examination method of research. In addition to establishing credibility in society, it should also popularize medical common sense among the general public. 2. Physicians should not take treating diseases as the fundamental method, but should guide national health care and thoroughly improve the race. Therefore, it is hoped that all representatives will make special efforts after the meeting. 3. Study Chinese national medicines to promote our country's inherent culture. After the banquet, they went to Wuhan University to visit Luojia Mountain and tour Wuhan University. The school prepared refreshments to welcome them. Lü Zhenming Suddenly Assassinated - Shot by Four Thugs While Playing at a Friend's House 122

Lü Zhenming (also known as Lü Xiaoerzi), a native of Jiangbei, thirty years old, residing at No. 23, Lane 587, Thomyot Hervé Road, was playing at the home of his friend Yang Bangjie in the garret of No. 60, Tong'an Lane, on the same road at around 7:00 PM on the 9th of this month, when four thugs suddenly arrived. Two of them, holding guns, broke into Yang's house and, without asking questions, shot at Yang and Lü, who were wounded and fell to the ground. The police arrived at the scene after hearing the news, but the murderers had disappeared without a trace. An ambulance was summoned to the scene to fly Yang and Lü to Baolong Hospital for treatment. The Gordons Road Police Station ordered Chief Detective Gao Huiguang and others to investigate. Since Lü and Yang were not good people, the reason for this assassination was due to infighting, and the criminals intended to silence them. Therefore, the detective immediately detained Yang's wife, Ms. Jin, and sent her to the First Special Court, requesting detention. Rescue was ineffective, and she died. The corpse was taken to the Phélan Road autopsy room. Although Yang suffered abdominal injuries, there was no danger to his life. Yesterday morning, Tang Prosecutor of the First Special Court, accompanied by forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zuyi, etc., went to the morgue to verify the corpse. Ms. someone, the wife of the deceased, had also fled. Mr. Tang then instructed that the autopsy showed that the deceased Lü Zhenming was male and died from gunshot wounds. The corpse was handed over to Pushan Villa for collection.

Jin Jutai Sand Boat Suddenly Disappears - Body of the Boat Exploded and Sank to the Bottom of the Sea - No Trace Seen Recently, Probably Washed Away 123

The Shandong Shijia sand boat Jin Jutai loaded raw oil, soybean cakes, and other cargo from Beikou to Shanghai for sale. At the end of November last year, when it approached the sea off Wusongkou, the helmsman neglected to steer, and the boat hit a buoy set up by the customs, the body of the boat exploded, the cabin flooded, and the boat and cargo immediately sank to the bottom of the sea. Sixteen crew members on the entire boat were fortunate to escape. Mr. Liu, a cargo owner, suffered heavy losses. At that time, due to the deep and wide water at the sinking location, it was impossible to salvage. Therefore, the total loss of the boat and cargo was about more than ten thousand yuan. According to customs officials, the sunken boat was once discovered not long ago, but recently, there has been no trace of the boat on the coast, probably due to the erosion of the waves or the impact of high tides and huge waves, and it has drifted elsewhere.

Zhang Tang Cried Out for Thieves and Was Shot - Burglary Occurs in Pengpu Township - The Security Team Did Not Arrive in Time 124

The peasant Zhang Yongchang, who lives in Pengpu Township, was suddenly robbed by four armed bandits at around 5:30 AM yesterday morning. At that time, Zhang's mother, Tang, sixty-six years old, had just woken up from sleep and saw many unfamiliar men pouring in. Knowing that things were not good, she hurriedly put on her clothes and got out of bed, ran out quickly, and shouted for thieves. When the bandits saw that things were difficult to accomplish, they turned back and exited, and saw a bicycle in the corner of the house, so they grabbed it and rushed out of the outer room. But at this time, Tang was still shouting wildly. In desperation, the bandits fired a shot at her, hitting her left shoulder, and she fell to the ground on the spot. The bandits were able to escape leisurely. Security team members nearby heard the gunshots and rushed to the scene, but it was too late to pursue them. They sent Tang to the hospital for treatment and cooperated with the police station to search for the culprits everywhere.

Jiangbei Fellow Associations Initiate the Establishment of a Joint Office 126

The original letter said: Respected Sirs, we have found that in recent years, due to floods, droughts, and robberies in various counties in Jiangbei, rural areas have gone bankrupt, and the number of fellow villagers who come to Shanghai to make a living has been increasing day by day. Usually, they are scattered and unorganized, and are often bullied and humiliated by foreigners. There is no way to complain about their grievances. There are also those who are unemployed, destitute, sick, and dead, and there is a lack of assistance and relief. The sight is heartbreaking, and there are rumors from time to time. Although each county has a fellow association in Shanghai, due to the large number of people and affairs, it is not possible to take care of everyone. Our association, etc., has realized this, so we initiated the establishment of a joint office of fellow associations in Shanghai from various counties in Jiangbei to unite and help each other to promote the strength of unity, so as to help each other in the same boat and benefit our fellow villagers. We have always admired your association for its years of establishment and its great concern for seeking the welfare of fellow villagers living here. We hope that you will sympathize with the establishment of this joint office, and we dare to invite your association to join the initiation, so that we can convene a joint meeting on a regular basis to discuss how to proceed. We hope that you will investigate and reply.

Ye Ruyuan, the elder brother of Ye Ruyu, a well-known Shanghai Sutan female opera singer, is over thirty years old. The petitioner is only willing to pay the respondent 100 yuan for damages, while the respondent's side means that they will not allow the divorce unless they return 500 yuan. Relatives and friends are now making every effort to mediate. It is still difficult to predict whether this matter can be settled outside the court and avoid litigation.

Wu Shouquan Was Defrauded in Xiamen While Selling Xiangzai Lottery Tickets on Consignment - The Subject Is Unclear and Cannot Be Verified 129

Wu Shouquan, a native of Siming, Fujian, thirty-five years old this year, used to open Dachuan Silver Company at the intersection of Zhongshan Road and Shuixian Road in Xiamen, operating banking business, and also selling the current lottery tickets. In October of last year, he received a letter from Sun Houcheng, the owner of Heji Shenzhuang, No. 33 Chengyu Lane, Lafayette Road, French Concession, Shanghai, saying that Heji Shenzhuang was selling Hunan Xiangzai relief lottery tickets on consignment, soliciting Wu to promote the Xiangzai lottery ticket business in Xiamen. Wu immediately replied and agreed to sell on consignment. Sun then sent Wu 500 eighth-term Xiangzai relief lottery tickets on November 25, and continued to send 1,000 ninth-term Xiangzai relief lottery tickets on December 25. After receiving these lottery tickets, Wu sold them in Xiamen, and remitted the ticket price of 440 yuan in cash. But when Wu was selling the second batch of lottery tickets, he found that these lottery tickets were forged, so he informed Heji Shenzhuang and negotiated with Sun. Sun replied that these lottery tickets were purchased from Liji Company in Hankou, etc. Wu then reported this to the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce and sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government for investigation, but to no avail. He also telegraphed Hankou to trace Liji Company, and received a reply denying that it had sold Xiangzai lottery tickets. People in Xiamen who bought lottery tickets negotiated with Wu one after another, causing Wu to be implicated and suffer heavy losses. When he came to Shanghai in person to seek out Sun for investigation, he was also troubled by not seeing Sun in person, and there was no Heji Shenzhuang at No. 33 Chengyu Lane. Wu then hired Tang Youwei as a lawyer to file a self-lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court based on the location of Heji Shenzhuang's letters received in the past, accusing Sun Houcheng of forging lottery tickets and defrauding property, requesting the court to investigate and punish him according to Articles 211 and 339 of the Criminal Law, and attaching a civil lawsuit, requesting to recover the defrauded ticket price of 440 yuan, etc. According to the petition, the court summoned the plaintiff in the Criminal Court yesterday by Criminal Court President Wang Gangxu. Because he had returned to Xiamen, the agent lawyer came to court to state the facts of the case and presented the correspondence. The defendant no longer lived at the original address and could not be served with a summons, so he did not appear in court. The plaintiff's lawyer also stated that the defendant had fled since this incident, and requested that he be allowed to be wanted or that an arrest warrant be issued to bring him to court for investigation. After reviewing the documents submitted to the court, the court decided that since the defendant's whereabouts were unknown, it was impossible to detain him, and the subject of the crime was unclear, so it was ordered to postpone the case and ordered the plaintiff to visit and investigate the defendant's whereabouts and then file a petition to the court for review.

Sino-French Friendship Association to Hold Literary Award Competition 133

The Sino-French Friendship Association believes that French literature is world-renowned. Therefore, to promote cultural exchange between China and France and improve Chinese drama, it has specially allocated 500 national currency to be used as this year's university scholarship to encourage talent. It also plans to hire well-known figures as judges to form a judging committee. The first-place winner will receive a prize of 300 national currency, and the second-place winner will receive 200 national currency, demonstrating the association's efforts in literature and art. The regulations are listed below:

In order to exchange Chinese and French culture and improve Eastern drama and art, this association has established a special literary award competition to foster interest. It will be held once a year. The award amount is set at 500 national currency, awarded for translated French drama scripts. The first prize is 300 national currency, and the second prize is 200 national currency.

The translated scripts participating in the literary award competition must be unpublished.

Participants in the literary award competition should submit their translations along with the original text to the association's secretariat before March 1st each year. However, the translator's name, address, and the title of the translated play should be stated on a separate sheet of paper, sealed, and sent to the association along with the translation. The translations will not be marked with names.

The association's directors will hire 10 to 15 committee members to form a judging committee to determine the awarding of prizes. The judging committee members are not limited to members of the association and will not participate in the competition.

The novelty of the original material and the value of the translation will both be used as standards for judging.

At the conclusion of the meeting, the judging committee will use multiple rounds of anonymous voting to decide the winners in order to show seriousness.

A public award ceremony will be held on May 30th each year to award the prizes.

Regarding the awarding of prizes, the judging committee has the independent right to decide. When necessary, it may decide to award prizes only in certain years or to stop awarding prizes altogether. The prizes left over from the previous item will be added to the prizes awarded in the following year.

Within its capabilities, the association will endeavor to publish the winning translations and make them performed.

Miscellaneous News 143

Pig Vendor Entrusts 50 Yuan, Goes Missing

Gu Demao, a 40-year-old man from Yangzhou, recently came to Shanghai from his hometown to sell pigs. Through the introduction of Chen Tingfang from Rugao, he sold the pigs to Changshun Pig Company, receiving 56 yuan, 3 jiao and 4 fen in legal tender. After receiving the money, Gu hid some of the money on his person and planned to visit Shanghai for a few days. He entrusted the remaining 50 yuan to Liu Dahu, a fellow villager, to take back to his home in Yangzhou. Unexpectedly, Liu had ulterior motives and embezzled the entrusted money. It was not until Gu returned home that he learned that the money had not been delivered. He rushed back to Shanghai and found Liu Dahu yesterday, taking him to the police station for investigation.

Children in Jiangsu Province Donate Candy Money to Cast Golden Sword to Present to Chairman Chiang 146

Xuzhou, 11th - When the Copper Commissioner's Office held a children's speech contest at the beginning of the year, Hu Xing Su, a female student from the attached elementary school of Xuzhou Normal School, proposed that children in Jiangsu Province save candy money to cast a treasure sword to present to Chairman Chiang, as a way to ask Chiang to command the people to resist insults and kill the enemy. It requested the Copper Commissioner's Office to ask the Education Department to order each county's elementary schools to collect one copper coin from each student. After the joint signature of more than 30 students, including Zai Xiuying, the Copper Commissioner's Office has drafted a method to be submitted to the Education Department for handling. It stipulates that the sword blade should be made of pure steel, and the scabbard should be made of 90% pure gold. It will be cast by the Education Department, and the sword will be engraved with words. Each county will propose four words, and the Education Department will adopt them. It is scheduled to be presented to Beijing by children representatives selected from the provincial capital on May 5th.

Elementary Schools in Various Counties in Anhui Province to Promote the Primary Two-Part System This Year 147

In order to promote compulsory education, Anhui Province, in addition to allocating funds within the compulsory education funds for the 24th year [1935] to subsidize the establishment of short-term elementary schools and the improvement of private schools, will uniformly teach short-term elementary school courses, and in the current year (24th year [1935]), it will hold a total of 230 classes of the primary two-part system in public and private single elementary schools in various counties. Each class will be subsidized by the province with 50 yuan. The number of children in the two-part system in the elementary schools in each county should increase by at least 30 children in addition to the original number of students in the school in the first semester to be able to start a class. All classes will start from the first grade. The students enrolled will receive the same treatment as the original students. The elementary schools implementing the two-part system may adopt an intermittent two-part system or a half-day two-part system.

Sino-French Association to Hold a Literary Prize Competition with an Annual Award of 500 Yuan 156

The Sino-French Association, recognizing the prominence of French literature worldwide, aims to foster Sino-French cultural exchange and improve Chinese drama. To this end, it has allocated 500 yuan in national currency for an annual literary prize to encourage such efforts. The association plans to engage renowned figures to serve on an evaluation committee. Winners will receive 300 yuan for first place and 200 yuan for second place, demonstrating the association's commitment to literary and artistic endeavors. The competition regulations are as follows: Sino-French Association Literary Prize Regulations. The association is holding a literary prize competition to promote cultural exchange between China and France and to improve Eastern drama. This will be held annually with a prize fund of 500 yuan in national currency. A first prize of 300 yuan and a second prize of 200 yuan will be awarded to the best translations of French plays into Chinese. Submitted translations for the literary prize competition must be unpublished. Participants in the literary prize competition must submit their translations, along with the original text, to the association's secretariat before March 1st each year. The translator's name, address, and the play's title should be indicated on a separate sheet, sealed, and submitted with the translation. Translations should be anonymous. The association's board of directors will appoint 10 to 15 committee members to form an evaluation committee for awarding the prize. Evaluation committee members need not be members of the association and may not participate in the competition. The originality of the source material and the value of the translation will both be considered evaluation criteria. The evaluation committee will make its decisions through anonymous voting during meetings to ensure impartiality. The awards ceremony will be held publicly on May 30th each year, during which the prize money will be awarded. The evaluation committee has the independent right to make decisions regarding the prize, and may decide to award only one prize or to suspend the award entirely if necessary. Any unawarded prize money will be added to the prize fund for the following year. The association will, to the extent possible, seek to publish the winning translations and have them performed.

Review and Outlook on Educational Administration (Part 2) - Lecture to be given on the Central Broadcasting Station at 5:30 PM on January 9th 160

— Lei Zhen

Holding of the Sixth National Games

The Sixth National Games was held at the Shanghai Municipal Central Stadium from October 10th to October 20th last year, lasting for eleven days. A total of 38 units participated, with over 2,700 male and female athletes, an unprecedented scale. The newly built Shanghai Municipal Central Stadium, with its magnificent architecture and complete facilities, is unmatched in the Far East and greatly enhanced the event. Since the opening ceremony, the total expenditure was 150,000 yuan, and many national records were broken in the men's and women's mountain cross-country races. This is sufficient to prove that China's sports have made considerable progress.

Organization of Educational Broadcasting

Recognizing the importance of radio broadcasting for education, the Ministry of Education organized educational broadcasts starting on October 10th last year. It first trained radio operators within the ministry and then ordered secondary schools and public education centers in various provinces and cities to install receivers in phases so that secondary school students and the general public throughout the country could have the opportunity to receive these broadcasts. All broadcasting lecturers are experts with rich knowledge and experience, and the selected teaching materials are essential knowledge. Currently, this work is proceeding smoothly and will benefit China's educational future if continued.

What I have discussed above is a review of the general situation of central educational administration over the past year. As for the outlook for future administration, in my humble opinion, the following points should be noted:

In terms of higher education, regarding schools above the junior college level, attention should be paid to qualitative improvement rather than focusing on quantitative expansion. As of now, there are 111 colleges and universities nationwide, which is already a considerable number. The central task in the future should be to improve and enrich the existing schools in terms of quality. As for quantitative expansion, it does not seem necessary to expand significantly unless it is necessary for national and ethnic construction. As for qualitative improvement, the most important thing is to focus on academic research and seek the independence of Chinese academics. The Chinese nation should not only seek independence in politics and economics but also in academics, so that it can gain a foothold in the world. In the future, colleges and universities should seek to improve their standards and specialize in academic research to lay the foundation for academic independence. At the same time, the state should actively reward research and inventions to encourage them. One more point is that the government should cultivate specialized talents and academic talents and should also employ them as much as possible. This is the great way to store and use talents.

In terms of general education, every effort should be made to promote compulsory education and vocational education. The importance of compulsory and vocational education is recognized by everyone, and it is also recognized as the most urgent need at present. We have already talked about the promotion of compulsory education above, but it is only the beginning. We should make every effort to promote and expand it in the future to establish the foundation of compulsory education. Vocational education is education for production and is very important at present. We should actively find ways to promote and enrich it.

In terms of social education, the central task in the future is to promote public education and public sports. An effective method should be devised to implement it, so that the public can receive basic training and development in terms of knowledge and physique.

Although there have not been significant achievements in Mongolian and Tibetan education in the past, there are indeed good plans for planning. In the future, we should start with compulsory education in the border areas according to these plans and then gradually seek the establishment of secondary normal schools and vocational education facilities so that we can achieve practical results. (End)

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1)(4)(9) 162

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"He didn't, but if he did, I'd stand up for him. He's always been good to me," Ned said, so sincerely that Don forgot his spider and immediately wanted to get up and thank him. But Ned went on:

"I know Don did it. He gave you the money. It's no wonder, if he's been living by cutting locks of hair before, and only you know his background here," Ned said deliberately, trying to provoke him into revealing the truth.

His bad intentions had a partial success, because Ned shouted fiercely:

"If you say it again, I'll go tell Mr. Pei everything. I didn't want to gossip, but if you're going to implicate Don, then I won't hesitate to tell him."

"Then you're not only a thief and a liar, but also an ugly bad guy," Ned began to mock him deliberately, because Ned could endure all insults so well that Ned didn't believe he would dare to complain to the teacher for Don's sake.

I don't know what else he had to say, because before he could finish, an arm grabbed him from behind by the collar, pulled him violently over the wall, and with a splash, threw him into the middle of the stream, where the water splashed and sprayed everywhere.

"If you say it again, I'll press you into the water until you can't even open your eyes!" Don shouted, looking like a statue of a warrior, majestic and high-spirited, his feet straddling either side of the stream, looking down at the fallen boy.

"I was just joking," Ned said.

"You're an ugly bad guy, forcing Ned to be desperate. As long as I see you again next time, I'll soak you in the river. Get up and get out." Don said in a rage, his voice like thunder.

The gold market remained sluggish yesterday. Many parties watched and did not move forward, and the situation in the market was extremely weak. Although the 40-yuan mark was not broken again, the trend was difficult to be optimistic about. The demand and supply were even more fragmented in the morning, and the market was extremely sluggish. Foreign Exchange Rates Over the Past Year (Continued) 170

— Ci

Two

In 1935, the most important event in China's financial history was the promulgation of the Ministry of Finance's new currency law on November 3. This not only had a significant impact on China's currency system and national economy, but also stabilized foreign exchange, which was unprecedented in the history of foreign exchange changes. China was based on silver, and for more than ten years, foreign exchange was severely affected by the price of silver or the monetary policies of other countries. This not only caused inconvenience to importers and exporters, but also greatly harmed the stability of people's livelihoods and the development of industries. A review of the fluctuations in foreign exchange rates in recent years will illustrate the general situation.

Shanghai Telegraphic Transfer Exchange Rate Table for British Pounds, US Dollars, and Japanese Yen (Note 3)

In the autumn and winter of 1931, Britain and Japan successively abandoned the gold standard, and foreign exchange rates saw a slight increase (but not very significant). In 1933, the United States also broke away from the gold standard. In these years, various countries devalued their currencies, all by about 40% to 60% below the old prices. China's foreign exchange rates should have risen accordingly, but in reality, the increase was minimal. It was not until 1934 that the rise occurred in Shanghai. In May 1935, the British pound reached 20.125 pence, the highest price in five years, but it still fluctuated from time to time. It was not until November 3 that the government announced the new currency regulations, adopting the pegging method, stabilizing the British pound at 14.5 pence, the US dollar at 29.75 yuan, and the Japanese yen at 103 yuan, and it has not been changed to this day. However, there are two points that deserve our special attention:

In the first half of this year, China was affected by the depreciation of foreign exchange rates and the increase in the price of silver, and the foreign exchange rates began to rise sharply. The high price in May had offset the extent to which China's foreign exchange rates had fallen due to the decline in the price of silver, and restored the normal state of 1929—that is, 20.524 pence. The promulgation of the Ministry of Finance's new currency law on November 3 opened the era of China's foreign exchange management, and foreign exchange rates will have a stable trend in the future.

The determination of China's foreign exchange rates is based on the London large-bar price, that is, the fixed number of taels of pure silver contained in each unit of China's currency is multiplied by the London large-bar silver price on that day, which will be the exchange rate for the British pound on that day (the exchange rates for other countries are calculated based on the British pound, using cross rates). However, since the United States raised the price of silver, China's foreign exchange rates have not in fact risen in equal amounts with the increase in the price of silver, so phenomena such as the outflow of silver have occurred. The following compares the situation of the London silver price and China's foreign exchange rates this year (Note 4): (To be continued)

Children's Special

What Kind of Person Will I Be in the Future? 185

— (First Prize in the Newspaper Essay Contest) Qiu Zhengxi, Chengbei Elementary School, Yiqu District, Jiangdu County, Jiangsu

Some people say that the reason why Chinese people are oppressed by foreigners is entirely due to the underdevelopment of science. This is very true.

Nowadays, all kinds of undertakings in the world are related to science. Because foreign countries have developed science and prospered industry, they are rich and powerful, so they can oppress our weak and small nations with backward science. If we want to resist the powerful and restore our free and equal status, we can only defeat them by developing science. Therefore, I am willing to be a scientist in the future, to fulfill my responsibility as a national.

But I am not willing to be a scientist who only knows how to invent artillery and poison gas to kill human beings. I am willing to be a scientist who is beneficial to the people, society, the country, and the world.

Like Pasteur in France, I will study and improve the agriculture and sericulture of my country, so that the harvest is abundant, the quality is excellent, and it is easy to sell to foreign countries.

Like Edison in the United States, I will invent many machines that use electricity as the driving force of industry, so that the products are cheap and good, and a lot of money can be made. Pasteur made France rich and powerful, Edison made the United States rich and powerful, and I also want to make China rich and powerful. But it is useless to just talk about it. I am now an elementary school student. I must work hard to learn, without interruption for a day. I must do it according to the following two methods:

(1) I must strive to study with my eyes anytime and anywhere, not completely relying on books. All phenomena in nature, such as the changes of cold and heat, the growth of all things, etc., must be recorded day by day as research materials.

(2) I must start with small things and gradually study big problems. For example, Newton saw an apple fall and knew about gravity, and Watt saw a lid overturn and invented the steam engine. These are the research spirits that I should emulate.

If all the elementary school students in the country can have the same ambition as me, and my ambition is achieved in the future, China will also become rich and powerful. At that time, what is there to fear of the oppression of imperialism?

This magazine received a letter from Mr. Qiu's parents a few days ago, saying: "The prize money of fifty yuan has been decided to be used to purchase children's books for the school library, as a permanent memorial for our library...:" We think the method is excellent, and after admiring it, we specially publish it as above. (Editor)

Tap Water 186

— Zhen

On Sunday, Min'er, in addition to reviewing his homework, had nothing to do, and asked his brother Cong'er to go to the bustling city to play with him. This was not the first request. So Cong'er agreed to him, so the two brothers walked to the city.

Before long, they had arrived at their destination. Min'er felt it was really fun. The shop windows on all sides were displaying colorful and bizarre things, making Min'er unable to see them in detail, and he kept asking his brother: What is this thing? What is that thing called? Cong'er was laughing at his brother's ignorance, but it was no wonder him, he had never seen these things before.

Gradually, they arrived at the entrance of a restaurant. Min'er saw a person turning on the tap, and clean water flowed out very quickly. Min'er was stunned, and quickly asked his brother:

"Brother, look, how can there be water coming out of that tap?"

"That water comes from the waterworks. There are many large water-pumping machines in the factory that can pump water from the river into very high water storage tanks. Some people call it a water tower. Then the water is distributed to everyone's homes through other iron pipes, but before it is sent to everyone's homes, there are many steps of work, such as disinfection and chemical testing, to know whether the water is clean, otherwise, it is easy to spread diseases."

"How does water come down from the water tower?"

"This is the use of the siphon effect. A siphon is a curved tube with unequal arms that can transfer water from a high place to a low place without having to pour the container. You think the water tower is so big, how can you pour the water tower? You can only use the siphon effect. In short, how does water come down from the water tower? It depends on the pressure of the air."

"I don't believe it!" Min'er said suspiciously.

"Okay, let's go home and try it for you." So the two quickly ran home.

Cong'er took a rubber tube and two bowls. He put one bowl in a high place and the other bowl in a low place, and then put the two ends of the tube into the bowls. The bowl in the high place had been filled with water, so he sucked the low end of the tube, and the water came down continuously. He said, "This is a siphon, as for the pen cap sucking water, the rubber tube in the fountain pen, this is also a siphon, but it is a metamorphosis."
